May 23, 1930 (Shen Bao Second Sheet) Friday (8)

Quiet News from Caozhou Battlefront

Jinan dispatch: Today, news from the Caozhou area is unusually quiet. It is said that Han Fuju and Ma Hongkui are still commanding military operations in Yuncheng. Ma's troops have been completely concentrated in Yuncheng from Tai'an, pushing forward on the northwest and west sides of Yuncheng, first clearing the south bank of the Yellow River, and then crossing the river northward. Chen Tiaoyuan is still in Juye. Fan Xiji's 46th Division and Ruan Zhaochang's 55th Division are currently near Heze and Dingtao, intercepting Shi Yousan's troops. Shi himself seems to be in the Heze area. Jiang Bocheng, the chief advisor of the headquarters, originally planned to go to Yuncheng to meet with Han Fuju, but Han telegraphed that he would return to Jinan within days, so Jiang stopped his trip. There is no fighting in the Yucheng area in northern Shandong. However, since the outbreak of the military conflict, all boats on the Yellow River have been ordered to dock to prevent the enemy from crossing, which has created problems for the livelihood of boatmen. Today, the provincial government's standing committee decided that boatmen stranded in various places will be given a living allowance of one jiao per person per day by the local county government.

The boatmen in Luokou will be paid by the Jinan Municipal Government after receiving funds from the Department of Finance. (May 20th)

High Court Judgment on the Gao Ying Case

After the Jiangsu High Court rendered a judgment on the Gao Ying appeal case on the 17th of this month, the full text of the judgment was delivered today (the 22nd). It is transcribed as follows:

"Criminal Judgment of the Jiangsu High Court, (19th Year Su Zi No. 376) Appellant: Jiangning District Court Prosecutor; Appellant: Gao Ying, male, 35 years old, from Changle County, Fujian Province, residing at Hefeng Lane, Jiaozhou Road, Shanghai; Former Vice Consul of the Consulate General of San Francisco, Gao Liao Shi, female, 24 years old, from Huiyang County, Guangdong Province, residing at the same address; Appointed Defense Attorneys: Wang Youling, Attorney-at-Law, Liu Shifang, Attorney-at-Law; Defendant: Sun Yuan, male, 40 years old, from Zhongshan County, Guangdong Province, residing in San Francisco, USA, former Chief Clerk of the Consulate General of San Francisco; Appointed Defense Attorneys: Li Zongqian, Attorney-at-Law, Hu Zhen, Attorney-at-Law. The above-listed appellants, Gao Ying et al., filed an appeal against the first-instance judgment of the Jiangning District Court on November 11, 18th year of the Republic of China, in the case of Gao Ying et al. concerning opium and dereliction of duty. After hearing the appeal, this court renders the following judgment: The original judgment is reversed. Gao Ying is sentenced to five years of imprisonment and a fine of 5,000 yuan for the crime of attempted assistance in opium trafficking, and three years of imprisonment and a fine of 3,000 yuan for the crime of soliciting bribes in connection with his official duties. The sentences of imprisonment shall be executed for a total of six years, and the total fine shall be 6,000 yuan. Gao Liao Shi is sentenced to four years of imprisonment and a fine of 4,000 yuan for the crime of attempted assistance in opium trafficking. Sun Yuan is sentenced to five years of imprisonment and a fine of 5,000 yuan for the crime of attempted assistance in opium trafficking. The number of days of detention before the judgment becomes final shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for each day of imprisonment. If the fine is not paid in full, each three yuan shall be converted into one day of imprisonment, but the term of imprisonment shall not exceed one year. The two cans of opium are confiscated and destroyed by burning.

The facts are that Gao Ying (also known as Gao Qianzhai) served as the Vice Consul at the Chinese Consulate General in San Francisco, USA. Sun Yuan, the Chief Clerk of the consulate, was aware of the international practice that the luggage of consulate personnel and their families could be exempted from inspection upon entry. Taking advantage of this opportunity, he colluded with unscrupulous overseas Chinese Shou Nan Ruoyun and unscrupulous merchants Shen Guang Wen Yuxian in Hong Kong, and in the 18th year of the Republic of China, had Gao Ying's wife, Gao Liao Shi (also known as Gao Liao Chengsu), return to China and travel to Hong Kong to transport 2,299 cans of opium divided into eleven boxes, each bearing the seals of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government and the signature of the Consulate General of the Republic of China in San Francisco, as her own luggage. Sun Yuan then transferred the opium to the consignees Shou Nan (also known as Fushou, Ruoyun, etc.) in exchange for a large reward. However, when Gao Liao Shi arrived in San Francisco on the Tianyang Maru on July 5th of that year, the U.S. Customs had already detected the previous situation and detained the luggage Gao Liao Shi had brought. On July 8th of the same month, the boxes were opened and inspected, and the aforementioned opium and letters from Shen Guang Wen Yuxian to Sun Yuan Ruoyun Shou Nan were found. The U.S. court arrested Gao Ying and his wife and Sun Yuan and released them on bail pending trial. After repeated negotiations by Minister Wu in the United States, Gao Ying and the other two people, along with two cans of opium, photographs of the letters, and certificates from U.S. Customs officials, were sent back to China and handed over to the Jiangning District Court Prosecutor for investigation. It was also discovered that in April of the 17th year of the Republic of China, Gao Ying, at the request of Chen Yi, admitted to receiving four Chinese laborers, Mei Guang, Mei Geng, Wu Zhuo, and Lu Huan, who were going to the United States. They agreed to a reward of US$2,400 to US$3,000. On June 8th of the same year, Mei Guang et al. arrived at the port on the Siberia. Gao Ying boarded the ship to receive them and discovered that the passports had been forged and the name of the Mexican Consulate had been abused. Knowing that it was not feasible, he sent Mei Guang et al. back. The former Minister Shi in the United States reported the matter to the National Government for the record. The case was investigated together and transferred to the criminal court for trial and judgment. In addition to sentencing Gao Ying and Gao Liao Shi to respective criminal punishments, Sun Yuan was found not guilty. Gao Ying and Gao Liao Shi disagreed and filed an appeal. The original prosecutor also disagreed with the part of the judgment that found Sun Yuan not guilty and appealed.

The reasons are that the facts of the crime in this case can be roughly divided into two parts: one is the opium part, and the other is the dereliction of duty part. These will be explained separately below. (A) Regarding the opium part, it was found that during Gao Liao Shi's trip from China to the United States, U.S. Customs inspected the luggage and found 2,299 cans of opium paste in the eleven boxes she was carrying. These facts are not only proven by certificates issued by U.S. Customs inspectors Harris and Smith, but also not denied by Gao Liao Shi, Gao Ying, Sun Yuan, and others. What should be investigated now is who owns the opium, whether it was transported to the United States for sale, and if it was transported on behalf of someone, whether Gao Liao Shi was aware of it and whether Gao Ying and Sun Yuan were involved. All of these are issues that should be resolved in this case and will be explained separately below. First, who owns the opium? It was found that there were a total of four letters found by U.S. Customs in Gao Liao Shi's own boxes. One was a letter jointly signed by Wen Yuxian and Shen Guang to Shou Nan, which stated, "Now the bearer is bringing two foreign boxes," and "These goods are all from Brother Shen Guang." The second was a letter solely signed by Shen Guang to Ruoyun, which stated, "Now Mr. Gao is bringing nine foreign boxes." The third was a letter jointly signed by Wen Yuxian and Shen Guang to Sun Yuan, which stated, "Please, brother, distribute the foreign boxes according to the letter to Brother Ruoyun and Shou Nan for receipt." The fourth was a letter solely signed by Wen Yuxian to Sun Yuan, with a similar meaning. It is certain that the opium was sent to the American overseas Chinese Shou Nan and Ruoyun by the unscrupulous Chinese merchants Wen Yuxian and Shen Guang. It was entrusted to Gao Liao Shi to carry it on their behalf and was not owned by Gao Liao Shi herself, which can be determined. Gao Liao Shi's claim that it was entrusted to her by Mr. and Mrs. Chen is not credible. Second, was it transported to the United States for sale? The letter from Wen Yuxian and Shen Guang to Shou Nan stated, "Now the bearer is bringing two foreign boxes, containing a certain number of K-branded Korean ginseng, with a cost of 85 yuan per branch and a carrying fee of 10 yuan per branch; a certain number of Chang-branded Korean ginseng, with a cost of 70 yuan per branch and a carrying fee of 5 yuan per branch." The fact that the seized opium cans had both K and Chang brands shows that the so-called Korean ginseng was clearly a euphemism for opium. Since the cost and carrying fee were indicated, it is clear evidence of sale. The letter also stated, "Please telegraph peace and the price as soon as the goods are received," and "If you remit silver, please send it to Guangdong Bank for Brother Shen Guang to receive it." The opium was transported to the United States for sale, which is undeniable. Third, was Gao Liao Shi aware that she was carrying the opium? Although Gao Liao Shi has consistently argued that the boxes containing opium were entrusted to her by Mr. and Mrs. Chen, and that she did not know that they contained opium, the boxes were originally sent by Wen Yuxian and Shen Guang to Ruoyun, as mentioned above. Gao Liao Shi claimed that they were entrusted to her by Mr. and Mrs. Chen, and could not provide the exact address of Mr. and Mrs. Chen. Her attempts to deceive are obvious. According to the letter from Shen Guang to Ruoyun, "Now Mr. Gao is bringing nine foreign boxes." The letter from Yuxian and Shen Guang to Shou Nan stated, "Now the bearer is bringing two foreign boxes." The so-called "Mr. Gao" and the so-called "bearer" both refer to Gao Liao Shi. The letter also stated, "The cost per branch is a certain amount of yuan, and the carrying fee per branch is a certain amount of yuan," and "Please pay the carrying fee according to the letter and do not overpay." The so-called carrying fee refers to the reward for carrying and transporting. The letter ended with "This carrying fee was agreed upon face-to-face between my brother and him." The "him" here clearly refers to the person carrying the opium, that is, Gao Liao Shi. Since she had personally contacted Wen Yuxian, Shen Guang, and others who were selling opium, and agreed on a reward before carrying and transporting it, how could she not know that it contained opium? She was greedy for the reward and provided direct and important assistance to Wen Yuxian and others in selling opium, which is beyond doubt. The boxes were affixed with the seals of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government and the signatures of the Consulate General of the Republic of China in San Francisco (as seen in the photographs of the boxes obtained from U.S. Customs), and Gao Liao Shi filled out the baggage declaration according to regulations as her own baggage (as admitted by Gao Liao Shi) in order to avoid inspection. The key to the box and the letters from Wen Yuxian, Shen Guang, and others were stored in her own box (as seen in the certificate from U.S. Customs officials). Gao Liao Shi's assisting behavior can be described as meticulous. To claim that she was unaware of the situation is a deception. Fourth, was Gao Ying involved in this opium case? The responsibility under criminal law can only be borne by the actor and cannot be imposed on someone other than the actor. Therefore, if Gao Ying was unaware that Gao Liao Shi was carrying opium for others, he cannot be held jointly liable solely because of the relationship between husband and wife. However, after reviewing the circumstances of this case, there are differences. Gao Ying was the Vice Consul, and his wife, Gao Liao Shi, was not an ignorant woman. If Gao Ying had not known about and condoned it in advance, she would not have done such an illegal and humiliating thing as the wife of a consul. Furthermore, the boxes carried by Gao Liao Shi were affixed with the Consulate's signature and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' seal. Since these seals and signatures were important conditions for carrying opium, if Gao Ying had not colluded in advance and issued them in advance, where would Gao Liao Shi have obtained them? Moreover, as soon as Gao Liao Shi's luggage was detained by U.S. Customs, Gao Ying immediately telegraphed Minister Wu, requesting negotiations for exemption from inspection and release. The telegram stated, "The box contains a small amount of drugs, which my wife was asked to bring by someone. For the sake of preserving the national integrity, it is absolutely forbidden to open it for inspection," (Telegram of July 5th). Before opening the box for inspection, Gao Ying sent another telegram to Minister Wu, urging him to negotiate. One said, "If it is opened for inspection, the national integrity will be completely lost. Please negotiate to have it destroyed." (Another telegram was sent in the name of Gao Liao Shi on July 7th, and two more telegrams were sent on July 8th). His panicked state had already been revealed in his words. After the opium was discovered after the inspection, Minister Wu ordered Consul General Gong Anqing to investigate. According to his reply, "Vice Consul Gao and his wife firmly refused to reveal the names of the people who contacted them in China and San Francisco, saying that they were afraid of unexpected retaliation." This is sufficient to show that there were people who contacted Gao Ying in China and San Francisco. According to the aforementioned seized letters, the people who contacted him in China were Shen Guang and Wen Yuxian, and the people who contacted him in San Francisco were Shou Nan and Ruoyun. The reason why Gao Ying and his wife were unwilling to announce their names at the time was that U.S. Customs had not yet announced the letters found in Gao Liao Shi's boxes, and they were afraid of unexpected retaliation if they announced them in advance. From the above-mentioned circumstances, comprehensively observed, it is very clear that Gao Ying used the opportunity of being a consul, colluded with his wife, and provided direct and important assistance to merchants selling opium. Fifth, was Sun Yuan involved in this opium case? Although Sun Yuan claimed that he knew nothing about Gao Liao Shi's carrying of opium, and that he did not know Wen Yuxian, Shen Guang, Shou Nan, Ruoyun, and others, the letters found in Gao Liao Shi's luggage to be handed over to Sun Yuan included one jointly signed by Yuxian and Shen Guang, which stated, "Now the bearer is bringing foreign boxes No. 1 to No. 9, a total of nine boxes, to Brother Ruoyun for receipt, and two foreign boxes to Brother Shou Nan for receipt. When they arrive at the port, please distribute the foreign boxes according to the letter to Brother Ruoyun and Brother Shou Nan. After handing over the foreign boxes, please telegraph peace." The other was solely signed by Wen Yuxian, which stated, "Please open the foreign boxes in person and check that boxes No. 2 and No. 11 are handed over to Brother Shou Nan for receipt, and the rest should be handed over to Brother Fu." Although the opium was carried to the United States by Gao Liao Shi, it still had to be transferred by Sun Yuan. According to the wording of the letters, it was not polite at all, not only entrusting him to transfer it, but also requesting a telegram reply, which is sufficient to show that both parties granting and receiving had extremely close relations with Sun Yuan, and even more sufficient to show that they had contacted him beforehand. Otherwise, why would Wen Yuxian, Shen Guang, and others rashly entrust a stranger with opium worth millions to transfer? Moreover, since the address of the consignee was not specified in the letter, if Sun Yuan did not know Ruoyun and Shou Nan, how could the opium be transferred separately? Moreover, since the opium had been carried to the United States by Gao Liao Shi, if it had nothing to do with Sun Yuan, it could have been delivered directly by Gao Liao Shi or Gao Ying, which would have achieved its purpose. Why would it necessarily need to be transferred by Sun Yuan? From the situation of this transfer that must be delivered by transshipment, it can be proven that Sun Yuan was one of the intermediaries in the contact. Although the original letter did not contain any words of prior contact, judging from the tone of the entire article, it is extremely clear that there was prior contact. Or it can be said that since the opium was detained as soon as it arrived in the United States, Sun Yuan's transfer behavior could not be realized, that is, his behavior of assisting in the sale had not yet begun. However, there is considerable evidence of Sun Yuan's prior contact and introduction. This behavior cannot be said to be non-assisting behavior merely because the opium was seized and could not be transferred afterwards. Based on the above explanation, Gao Ying, Gao Liao Shi, and Sun Yuan all had prior contact with Wen Yuxian and others in the sale of opium, and they all used international practices to provide direct and important assistance to unscrupulous merchants selling opium as consular personnel. Some carried it to the country for them, and others made plans in the United States to respond. They divided the work and cooperated, and their uses were equal. Those who acted and those who stayed were equally guilty. However, because it was discovered midway, and Wen Yuxian and others did not achieve the purpose of selling, Gao Ying, Gao Liao Shi, Sun Yuan, and others only committed the crime of attempted assistance in opium trafficking. (To be continued)

Jiangxi Bandit Suppression Headquarters Moves to Nanxun Road

From Zhangshu to Tujiapu

Nanchang dispatch: Since Jiangxi Province was divided into two major bandit suppression defense zones, two brigades of the 18th Division, one brigade of Cheng Guangyao, and Chen Lei's regiment have moved to northern and western Jiangxi. The 12th Division and the newly formed 13th Division have moved to southern and eastern Jiangxi, and are carrying out suppression according to plan. However, the General Headquarters for Bandit Suppression of the entire province was originally stationed in Zhangshu Town. This place can take care of southern and western Jiangxi, but it is beyond its reach for northern Jiangxi. Now, Zhang Huizan believes that Nanxun Road in northern Jiangxi is the throat of transportation in the province. Recently, it has been repeatedly cut off and destroyed by bandits, and Xiushui and Ruichang have also been captured by bandits. He urgently needs to supervise the suppression in person to consolidate the province's gateway. Therefore, yesterday he led the entire staff of the headquarters from Zhangshu to the province, and today took the Nanxun Road train to Tujiapu, which is located in the middle of the Nanxun Road (within Yongxiu). The command is also very convenient. Currently, the 103rd Regiment and the Engineer Battalion have been stationed along the Nanxun Road. Zhu Yaohua's brigade is also stationed in the Tongwan area, and Xiushui has been recaptured. Chen Lei's regiment is stationed in the Wurui area, suppressing the bandits in Ruichang. After the Bandit Suppression Headquarters is deployed in Tupu, Zhang Huizan plans to go to various places in northern Jiangxi to inspect the defenses. As for the defense of Zhangshu, it is temporarily the responsibility of Deng Ying of the New 13th Division. (20th)

Black River and Ussuri River Merchant Ships Test Navigation

Naval Forces Clear Mines from the Three Rivers Estuary

Northeast Shipping Bureau Merchant Ships Test Navigation to Open Routes

Harbin Correspondence: After the ice melted on the Songhua, Heilong, and Ussuri Rivers this year, in addition to the regular boat service from Fujin to Harbin on the Songhua River, the Sino-Russian disputes over the Eastern Railway last year led both countries to lay mines at the Three Rivers Estuary. Before the mines were cleared, merchant ships were naturally hesitant. Therefore, since navigation began in late April, no ships had ventured on the Black River and Ussuri River. Recently, the River Defense Fleet Command dispatched Fan Xishen, the former captain of the Jiang'an warship, with over twenty naval personnel, on a Northeast Shipping Bureau ship to inspect the waterways at the Three Rivers Estuary and observe Russian activities. Aside from two Russian warships stationed near Xu'erwei, there was no significant activity. Realizing that navigation on the Black River and Ussuri River might proceed without incident, he supervised the naval personnel in removing the mines inside and outside the Three Rivers Estuary. He also telegraphed the Northeast Shipping Bureau in Harbin, which relayed the information to the various shipping companies. Upon receiving the news, the companies prepared to operate ship services on the Black River and Ussuri River. The Black River route will temporarily terminate at Heihe, and the Ussuri River route will terminate at Hulin. It was decided that the Northeast Shipping Bureau's Suzhou ship would conduct a test voyage on the 16th of this month. After the Suzhou ship sets sail, several other merchant ships will follow, maintaining a distance of two days' voyage. If the Suzhou ship encounters misfortune, the subsequent ships will be able to stop sailing. The Naval River Defense Command has also ordered the river defense ships Lishui, Jiangqing, and Liji to anchor between Fujin and Tongjiang to provide assistance in case of emergency. According to the shipping industry, the only concern for merchant ships venturing out of the Three Rivers Estuary is the risk of uncleared mines. The Sino-Russian negotiations on navigation rights only involve the long-pending issue of Chinese ships navigating out to sea via Nikolayevsk-on-Amur (a treaty port), with no other problems. The Black and Ussuri Rivers are jointly owned by China and Russia. According to international law and the new and old Sino-Russian treaties, both countries have freedom of navigation and neither should hinder or interfere. The publicly applicable navigation regulations were also established as early as 1928 by Zhang Shouzeng, the supervisor of the Hunchun Customs, and Mo Yumeide, the Russian consul in Heihe, along with relevant personnel from both sides, with the permission of both governments. They jointly organized the Sino-Russian Waterway Committee and stipulated ninety-six articles, which have long been implemented. Although Russia took various irregular actions last year during the Sino-Russian dispute, these were after the severance of diplomatic relations between the two countries. Now that diplomatic relations are gradually being restored, and an agreement has been reached to restore the peaceful state of the Sino-Soviet border as a prerequisite, the eastern and western routes have long been as peaceful as usual. Jointly owned rivers are still open to navigation, and there is no further question about it. However, the Sino-Soviet conference is currently being held in Moscow, and it is anticipated that the voyage of our merchant ships on the Black River and Ussuri River will not be dangerous. (15th)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Detailed Account of the Robbery at Shengzi Temple Town in Punan, Under the Jurisdiction of the County: Shengzi Temple Town in Punan, under the jurisdiction of the county, is located at the intersection of Songjiang and Fengxian, about six li away from Tinglin and Yexie. The commercial market is not prosperous, with only small-scale shops. There is a police station with six police officers, led by one patrol chief, under the jurisdiction of the First Branch Bureau of Tinglin. On that day (the 20th) afternoon, a gasoline boat towed two Wujiang boats was docked outside the town at San Cha Yang. The people on the boats looked like villagers. When the Songshan steamboat passed by, people on the Wujiang boats peeked and looked around, which was very suspicious. The townspeople warned each other. Unexpectedly, a robbery and police-killing incident occurred that night. It has been learned that there were about thirty to forty robbers who entered the town, each holding flashlights, box guns, pistols, and other weapons. Patrol Chief Cheng Ruyao of the police station, upon hearing the news, immediately led the police to resist. However, the robbers were numerous, and the police were few, and their weapons were not as sophisticated as those of the robbers. After a brief clash, Patrolman Xu Bin was shot and killed on the spot. Patrol Chief Cheng Ruyao was shot in the chest and flanks, wounded, and retreated. The robbers then split up and searched for valuables. They first entered the Nanhuo shop opened by the Sheng family and robbed it, then proceeded to rob other houses, lasting for two hours, carrying away the stolen goods with shouts. The town chief Sheng Huanzhang's house was also broken into by the robbers. It is estimated that seven families, including Yin Mengkui, Zhuang Ruizhi, Zhang Youliang, Hu Shaokang, Li Musheng, and Sheng Shaoyu, suffered losses, including rice shops, Nanhuo shops, and meat shops, with an estimated total loss of over a thousand yuan. Yesterday morning (the 21st), Pan Yongqiang, the director of the Tinglin Public Security Branch Bureau, reported to County Magistrate Jin by long-distance telephone and immediately appointed Team Leader Chen, Secretary Wang, Examination Official Tao, and other seven people to go to the countryside for investigation. They inspected the robbed households and examined the body of the slain patrolman Xu Bin. It was confirmed that Patrol Chief Cheng Ruyao was shot, with injuries to the chest and waist, and was seriously injured. Today he was taken to the Ruose Hospital in Songjiang for treatment. According to the doctor's diagnosis, his life is in grave danger. Team Leader Chen, Secretary Wang, and others returned to Songjiang after completing their duties and have reported the details to the county government. It is reported that the robbers fled southeast into Fengxian County after the robbery, and they came from this route as well. It is feared that they are from the Tai Bao Ah Xu's troops, who are staying in the Qianjiawei area. Now the military and police in Tinglin, Yexie, Shanyang, and Caojing are all on high alert.

Suzhou

Discovery of a Large Gang of Bandits in Nanxu Town: The area of Nanxu Hengjing in Wujiang County is located on the shores of Taihu Lake and has always been a haunt for lake bandits. The former Taihu Bandit Suppression Headquarters was established in Suzhou and ordered the bandit suppression army, navy, police, and other forces to be stationed at various key points. They repeatedly engaged in fierce battles with the bandits and dispersed them. Therefore, bandit activity in Nanxu and other places disappeared. In almost a month, the local area was able to enjoy peace. Unexpectedly, after the bandit suppression army was withdrawn, the bandits regrouped and formed a large gang. On the 21st, they gathered in the Nanxu Hengjing area of Wujiang County, with about three hundred bandits and more than twenty boats, fully equipped with guns and weapons. They also sent bandit scouts to secretly land and investigate the local situation. They also threatened to loot the towns along the lake. The Nanxu and other public security branch bureaus immediately reported to the Wujiang County Government and discussed with the Third Battalion of the Fifth Regiment of the Second Central Training Brigade stationed in Wujiang to request the dispatch of a team to advance and suppress the bandits, in order to avoid disturbing the local area. After receiving the report, Battalion Commander Ma immediately telegraphed Brigade Commander Luo stationed in Suzhou for instructions. After receiving the telegram, Brigade Commander Luo telegraphed the battalion commander yesterday (the 22nd), instructing him to immediately dispatch a team to patrol and suppress the bandits. If they encounter bandits, they should strike hard and not allow any to escape.

County Government Takes Over the Sheng Family's Estate: Due to the merger of the county and city, the secretariat of the city government has not yet been closed and handed over. It was completely closed yesterday (the 22nd), and all files were transferred to the county government for takeover. All the Sheng family's property held by the city government has also been transferred one by one. The county government specially appointed Director Qiao of the Social Affairs Bureau to take over the Liuyuan Garden property. After the takeover, it will still be allowed to remain open.

Bandits Rob and Injure People in Lishu Township: In Shujingqiao, Lishu Township, under the jurisdiction of the county, at about 3:00 AM the day before (the 21st), a bandit boat suddenly arrived with more than ten bandits. They immediately landed and robbed several families, including Zhou Renshan, Zhou Xiaomao, Zhou Changda, and Zhou Shuiquan. During the robbery, Zhou Renshan's wife was stabbed by the bandits with a knife. The bandits then fled. After receiving the report, Huang Xiongxiang, the head of the public security branch bureau in charge, came to the city yesterday (the 22nd) to report to the county government and request an arrest.

Nantong

Hu Battalion Achieves a Great Victory in Bandit Suppression in Yudong: After Yudong was repeatedly robbed by large groups of bandits, the Hu Battalion of the Fifth Division stationed in Erjia Town went to intercept them. The bandits fled to Huolong Town. The Hu Battalion's troops divided into three routes to encircle and suppress them. The artillery fire on both sides was very fierce. Over a hundred bandits were killed, and over two hundred surrendered. Three soldiers of the Hu Battalion were killed and two were wounded. The surrendered bandits were temporarily held at Sijia Dam. Battalion Commander Hu arrived in the city on the 21st to discuss follow-up measures with the county government and then went to Yudong to supervise the troops in pursuing the fleeing bandits.

County Government Requests Instructions on Handling Bandit Cases: County Magistrate Zhang stated that since the county court has been established, the county government no longer handles judicial matters. However, recently, bandit disturbances have occurred in the eastern townships, and the provincial and county police teams and the National Army have captured bandits and handed them over to the county government. He has specially submitted a report to the provincial government requesting instructions on how to handle the bandit cases.

Eastern Township Telephone Lines Temporarily Difficult to Repair: The eastern township long-distance telephone lines, extending as far east as Lusi Seaport, have had fifty telephone poles sawn down by bandits. Local military and political circles are raising funds to send craftsmen to repair them, and the work is currently underway. However, the telephone exchanges in Yudong and other districts have been completely destroyed, and it will be difficult to repair them in a short period of time.

Provincial Order to Inspect Mail: The provincial government, in accordance with a letter from the Provincial Rectification Committee, ordered the county government to increase the inspection of mail due to the rampant reactionary forces in the area and appointed Lin Kai as the director of mail inspection.

Sea Bandits Loot Ships on the Sea: The sea area of Tonghai, Chongming, and Hai'an counties is again turbulent. Sea bandits are looting merchant ships and fishing boats in the Lusi Pengjiatao area. It is reported that over forty ships have been looted. Zhu, the district chief of the Wusong Maritime Public Security Team, telegraphed the county magistrates of Tonghai and Chongming to send teams to cooperate in the suppression.

Tongshan

Zhang Xun's Rebel Ancestral Hall Ordered to be Used as a School Site: In this county, there is the ancestral hall of Zhang Xun, the leader of the restoration, the former residence of which is the site of the Provincial Xuzhou Women's Middle School Experimental Primary School, and the rear residence is the site of the Red Swastika Society. Last month, the principal of the school submitted a request to the Education Department to permanently use the former and rear residences of the rebel ancestral hall as the school site. The Education Department then submitted it to the Provincial Government Committee for discussion. It has been resolved to permanently use it as the school site. Today (the 21st), the Tongshan County Government was instructed to notify the Red Swastika Society to move out and report.

Local Correspondence Two

Wuxi

Re-survey of the Yichang Provincial Road Route: The Yichang Provincial Road is formed by the combination of the Xiyi Road (from Wuxi to Yixing) and the Xichang Road (from Wuxi to Changshu). The entire route starts from Yixing in the west, traverses this county, and ends in Changshu in the east. Since the general route was determined, it has been surveyed four or five times. The Construction Bureau of the Wuxi County Government originally planned to start recruiting labor to build the Xichang section in April of this year. However, due to the silkworm and farming seasons, the villagers along the route did not have time to respond to the recruitment. Therefore, County Magistrate Sun obtained approval from the Construction Department to postpone it until after the autumn harvest. Currently, the construction of bridge and culvert projects is planned first. Recently, Director Sun of the Construction Department believed that recruiting labor to build roads is a major construction project and that there are still many places that need to be re-surveyed on the route. He sent Jiang Housheng, the leader of the Provincial Highway Bureau's survey team, as the director of the Yichang Provincial Road re-survey. He came to Wuxi by car from the province the day before with three surveyors and eight laborers to carry out the re-survey. After arriving in Wuxi, he immediately contacted the Construction Bureau and will depart today or tomorrow to survey each section. In addition, the northern route of the Xiyi section of the Yichang Road is planned to utilize the Kaiyuan North Road from the city to Outang Bridge. Recently, Feng Genfu, Bian Zhenqing, and other residents of the Outang Bridge section and the Yangshuyuan section initiated the construction of a highway from Outang Bridge to Yangshuyuan as a branch road of the northern route of the Xiyi section. The route is eight li long, and the required funds are to be raised by the initiators. Once the funds are collected, they will submit a request to the county government for protection to facilitate transportation.

President Prince Chichibu Attends

22nd [of the month] - Tokyo Special Dispatch from This Newspaper: The Ninth Far Eastern Games will open tomorrow, Saturday. Approximately 600 athletes from the four participating countries will be present. Indian athletes are joining for the first time this year, participating in three sports. At noon on the opening day, Prince Chichibu, the president of the Games, will officiate the opening ceremony. Prime Minister Hamaguchi and other important figures will also attend. The ceremony will commence with twelve bell rings. The staff of the sports delegations from the four countries, led by a military band, will parade from the main gate to the venue, circling once around the field, and lining up in front of the command platform. Each team will have a flag bearer carrying their national flag. After the band plays the Japanese national anthem, Prince Chichibu will deliver an address, followed by the reading of a message from the Minister of Education. Next, Kishiseiichi will deliver the opening speech, and Prime Minister Hamaguchi will give a welcome speech. Finally, representatives from the four countries, including Zhang Boling, will deliver response speeches. The Games flag will then be raised on the main flagpole, completing the ceremony. The Emperor will not be in attendance.

British Embassy

Does Not Allow the Hanging of the Indian Flag

Only the Flag of the Governor-General of India May Be Displayed

Yesterday, Indian Athletes Strongly Opposed, Resulting in Neither Flag Being Hung

22nd [of the month] - Reuters Tokyo: The Indian athletes at the Far Eastern Games are lodging at the YMCA with the Chinese and Philippine athletes. The Chinese and Japanese national flags, as well as the Philippine government flag, are flying high on the flagpole of the building. In addition, the eye-catching red, green, and white flag of the Indian National Congress was also displayed. After two days, Japanese sports authorities consulted with the British Embassy. They received a reply stating that the flag of the Governor-General of India was the proper emblem. Therefore, the tricolor flag was taken down and replaced with the flag of the Governor-General of India. The Indian athletes strongly opposed this, and so the Governor-General's flag was also taken down. Today, the flagpole only displays the flags of China, Japan, and the Philippines, with one pole left empty, representing India. The Indian athletes stated that during the opening ceremony on Saturday, they would rather enter the venue without a flag than display the British flag.

22nd [of the month] - Tokyo Special Dispatch from This Newspaper: Regarding the dispute over the Indian flag, the Japanese authorities, after consulting with the British Embassy, decided to hoist the British flag. After the Indian representatives arrived, they protested, demanding that the Indian revolutionary flag be displayed. The Japanese authorities were greatly embarrassed. Negotiations are currently underway to take down the British flag in order to appease the Indian athletes. The public is eagerly awaiting a decision.

Practice of the Japanese Volleyball Team

China Has High Hopes

Can Win the Championships in Football, Volleyball, and Basketball

The Baseball Team is Feared by the Japanese

Qiu Lin's Tennis Skills Are Also Excellent

20th [of the month] - Tokyo Special Dispatch from This Newspaper: Japan is quite confident in winning the championships in athletics, the all-around event, and swimming, three of the eight competitions at the Far Eastern Games. As for tennis, Japan's top players, such as Harada, Ota, Abe, and Sato (the elder), have already been dispatched to Europe and the West to compete in the Davis Cup. Therefore, this year, Japan's representatives will still have to rely on the second-tier players Sato (the younger) and Bui. The two were previously defeated in Shanghai, and the tennis championship was won by our country. However, this year's championship is the most difficult to predict. Although Bui previously defeated Lin Baohua in Southeast Asia, the Japanese are quite wary of Qiu Feihai's skills. In baseball, Japan's Oda, who excels in the triple jump at the All-Japan Athletics Championships, is on the team, but the Japanese dare not say they are confident, because our country's team cannot be underestimated. Our country has the best chance of winning the championships in football, basketball, and volleyball. At this Games, our country can win at least three championships, as can Japan. If the two countries are equal, then the number of silver medals won will determine the victor. At the last Games, China and Japan each won three championships, but the Japanese also won three silver medals in football, tennis, and swimming, while our country only won two silver medals in baseball and basketball, so we failed. Our country has great hopes for this Games and a good opportunity to avenge our defeat. The Philippines will likely not be optimistic this time. The life-or-death battle belongs to China and Japan.

22nd [of the month] - Tokyo Special Dispatch from This Newspaper: The Minister of Education held a welcome reception in the afternoon, attended by over 500 people. Key representatives gave speeches and filmed a movie to commemorate the event.

Long Tickets for Baseball and Athletics Are Already Sold Out

Ordinary Tickets - Sixty Percent

Long tickets for baseball and athletics have almost sold out, and sixty percent of the tickets for other sports have also been sold. Chinese Cheerleading Squad

Purchasing Tickets Costs 800 Yen Daily

22nd [of the month] - Second Newspaper, Tokyo Special Dispatch: The Chinese cheerleading squad has also set aside 800 yen daily to purchase tickets.

Overseas Chinese in Kobe Raise Funds

Totaling 5,050 Yen

｜Extremely Enthusiastic｜

(This newspaper's Kobe correspondent on the 16th) Since the start of fundraising among overseas Chinese in Kobe, all sectors have supported it enthusiastically. Despite the difficult business conditions, they have been able to obtain a large sum, demonstrating the sincerity of the overseas Chinese in caring about their motherland and welcoming the Far Eastern Games athletes. Method of Competing for Championships

Eight Championships... The Country with the Most Wins is the Victorious Nation

(This Newspaper's Tokyo Communication) The sports events of the Far Eastern Games are divided into athletics

The Chinese Athlete Delegation's Sea Voyage to the East (II)

(Jointly recorded by Dong Shouyi, Wang Xiliang, and Sun Sijing on the Ocean Maru)

Athletes Vie to Get a Glimpse of Moji Port

May 16

In the morning, after washing and dressing, the athletes went out. In no time, the deck became another colony for the athletes. They lined up and gazed around the ship. Suddenly, they heard a bell, indicating that breakfast was ready. Before long, they respectfully entered the dining hall from the high ground. Over a hundred people dined at the same time, solemnly and neatly, which was truly commendable. The Japanese servants attending to the guests praised them endlessly, exchanging greetings. After the meal, the athletes rested and enjoyed themselves, which was very pleasant. At noon, because the sea was as smooth as a mirror, many people came out of their cabins to gaze into the distance. They saw huge fish emerging and disappearing from the water. At this point, the athletes hastened to get a better look. At eleven o'clock, the Executive Committee of the Chinese Delegation to the Far Eastern Games held a meeting. Zhang Boling was elected as the Executive Chairman, and seven committee members were elected, including Hao Boyang, Ma Yuehan, Rong Qizhao, Qiu Jixiang, Dong Shouyi, Mo Yinggui, and Xu Zhendong. The committee will be fully responsible for external negotiations and all important internal affairs related to this Games. At the same time, the secretary-general informed us that the ship will arrive in Kobe at around 4 pm tomorrow (the 17th). A notice was posted regarding matters after disembarkation, in order to remind all athletes. The text is as follows: Attention Chinese Team Members (1) Arrive in Kobe at approximately 4 pm tomorrow (the 17th). (2) Dinner will be served at 6 pm (the dining location will be announced later). (3) Take the 8 pm night train to Tokyo on the 17th, arriving in Tokyo at around 9 am on the 18th. (4) Report the number of luggage pieces to each team leader so that luggage can be urgently shipped by luggage car. (5) Small pieces of luggage can be managed by yourselves. (Secretary-General Rong Qizhao, Deputy Secretary-General Xu Zhendong) After tea in the afternoon, the athletes of each team did some light exercises to stretch their muscles and bones. In the ship's main hall, the film "Lilacs Blooming Everywhere" by "Kemur" was shown. The content was set against the backdrop of the European War, depicting the conditions of the trenches during wartime and the happy ending of lovers. It was said to be a very beautiful story. By the time it was over, it was already eleven o'clock. As the athletes were about to return to their rooms to sleep, they suddenly heard a whistle. Looking into the distance, they saw brilliant smoke. They asked the captain and learned that Moji Port was in sight. The athletes eagerly rushed to get a better look, but at this time, coach Shu Hong repeatedly urged the athletes to return to their rooms, as it was time to rest.

Newly Built Swimming Pool

Track, swimming, baseball, tennis, volleyball, football, basketball and other items. Since the last Shanghai Games, track and field has been divided into two championships. The one that is independent of track and field is called the all-around event, or mixed competition, which includes five events, ten events, and 800-meter and 1600-meter relays. Since the creation of the all-around event, the Games have been divided into eight championships. The country with the most championships is the victor, ranking first. The method of determining the winners of each competition is as follows: In track and field and swimming, four athletes are selected for each event. First place gets five points, second place gets three points, third place gets two points, and fourth place gets one point. However, in the swimming relay race, first place gets ten points, second place gets six points, and third place gets four points. If only two countries participate in this competition, then there is no third place. Only the first and second places are selected. The scores are added up to determine the winner. In baseball, volleyball, and basketball, each country plays a round-robin tournament twice. In football, each country plays once to determine the winner. Tennis follows the Davis Cup regulations. Each country plays four singles and doubles matches. The country that wins three matches wins the championship. At the last Games, our country won all four matches. Therefore, this year, Japan and the Philippines must compete first. The winner of the Japan-Philippines match will then play our country in the final. The scoring of the all-around event is the same as that of the swimming relay. In the five-event, ten-event, and 800-meter and 1600-meter relays, four athletes are selected. First place gets ten points, second place gets six points, third place gets four points, and fourth place gets two points. The scores of the athletes selected from each country are combined and tallied to determine the winner. The country that wins the most of the eight championships will be awarded the Taisho Emperor Cup and will retain it permanently if it wins three consecutive times. (Ruan Weicun)

Hangzhou Municipal Government Plans to Build a Public Stadium

The Hangzhou Municipal Government believes that the physical fitness of its citizens is weak, and that the promotion of physical education is an urgent matter at the present time. It has been found that the city has only three sports fields: the Provincial Public Stadium, the Municipal Children's Stadium, and the newly built National Stadium. However, the city area is vast, and the number of citizens is increasing. Therefore, there should be more places for the public to exercise. The city government plans to build a municipal public stadium in a suitable location in the city to promote public amateur sports and reduce the bad habits of citizens. This project will be organized by the Education Department of the Municipal Government to facilitate its progress.

Important News

Ministry of Education

Measures for Soliciting a National Anthem

The Ministry of Education previously drafted measures for soliciting a national anthem and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for review. The plan has now been approved and filed by the Executive Yuan of the National Government. The measures are extracted below.

Measures for Soliciting a National Anthem (1) Standards for Soliciting a National Anthem (1) The lyrics must be able to express national characteristics and common ideals in order to evoke patriotic concepts, national consciousness, and promote the spirit of the Three Principles of the People, so that the people know where to go. (2) The lyrics should be simple in language and rich in meaning, so that the people of the whole country, men, women, old and young, can recite them easily and spread them easily. (3) The lyrics should be sonorous in tone and uplifting, so that the people feel happy and encouraged when they sing. (2) Applicants must submit the lyrics clearly written by the end of August of the 19th year, and indicate the name and detailed address of the songwriter and submit it to the Social Education Department of the Ministry of Education. It is especially welcome if you can send the sheet music together. (3) After the national anthem manuscripts are collected, the Ministry of Education will invite advanced parties to evaluate and select them, and the results will be announced in September of the 19th year. (4) The Ministry of Education will award the winner 1,000 ocean dollars.

Before the 18th Year in Various Counties in Jiangsu

Measures for Clearing Education Funds

The Jiangsu Education Department ordered the promulgation of measures for clearing the accumulated deficits in education funds before the 18th year in various counties.

1. The accumulated deficits in education funds in various counties before the 18th year should be cleared in accordance with these measures and should not be mixed into the budget for the 19th year.

2. If there are accumulated deficits in education funds in various counties before the 18th year, the county magistrate should supervise the director of the Education Bureau to investigate the accumulated deficits and reasons in previous years in the following three situations, and list them for examination.

(1) Loans with mortgages or other guarantees should include the following items in the list, and fill in the total number at the end of the list (1) Loan date and the person in charge, (2) Name of the loan institution or private person, (3) Loan amount.

Japanese Swimming Preliminaries

Sada Tokuhei (Meiji University)

(4) Mortgage or other guarantee (5) Predetermined interest rate and repayment method (6) Whether it has been submitted for approval, (7) Reason for the loan, (8) Remarks, (2) Loans misappropriated from other funds should include the following items in the list, and fill in the total number at the end of the list, the date of misappropriation and the person in charge, (2) The nature of the misappropriated funds, (3) The amount of the misappropriation, (4) The original repayment method, (5) Whether it has been submitted for approval (6) Reason for the misappropriation, (7) Remarks, (3) Expenses owed to various schools and institutions, the following items should be listed separately for each year, and the total number should be filled in at the end of the list, (1) The school or institution that owes the money (2) The amount owed, (3) The reason for the debt (4) The budget of the agency has been submitted for approval, (5) Remarks,

3. The accumulated deficits in education funds in various counties before the 18th year shall be supervised by the county magistrate, together with the director of the Finance Bureau and the director of the Education Bureau, and the director of the Property Office, to formulate repayment steps and methods for the above table according to the urgency, and submit them for approval and implementation.

4. For all education funds that have not been collected or have been misappropriated before the 18th year, the county magistrate shall supervise the director of the Finance Bureau, the director of the Education Bureau, and the director of the Property Office to truthfully investigate and fill in the table, submit it for approval, and order the county magistrate to supervise the directors of each bureau to strictly pursue the recovery,

5. If the educational properties of various counties are occupied by private individuals or other groups or institutions, the county magistrate shall supervise the director of the Education Bureau to recover them and strictly liquidate them, and the expenses previously occupied.

6. If the past directors of the Education Bureau have not cleared their accounts or have privately misappropriated education expenses, the county magistrates shall follow the provincial orders to investigate and urge them to clear their accounts and recover the funds within the time limit, and submit a special case to the Department for handling. If the county magistrates delay in investigating and submitting reports, they shall order the county magistrates to be responsible for clearing the debts.

7. The income from the above items 4, 5, and 6 shall be given priority to clear the accumulated deficits in funds, and if there is still insufficient, the county magistrate shall be ordered to supervise the director of the Finance Bureau and the director of the Property Office to raise additional funds to make up for the deficit, and if there is a surplus, it shall be used as a fund.

8. Starting from the 19th year, if various counties still do not comply with the budget regulations and arbitrarily disburse funds, resulting in further deficits, the county magistrate and the director of the Education Bureau shall be jointly responsible, and this method shall not be used.

Suzhou Education Uprising Expands

The Municipal Education Director, Following the Teachers and Staff, Resigns En Masse

The teachers and staff of Suzhou City had previously presented a mass resignation due to three months of unpaid education fees and the lack of a responsible statement from the competent authority. All school affairs were maintained solely by the principals. Now the situation has escalated. Although the County Education Bureau has taken over the Municipal Education, it has only promised to allocate the unpaid salaries gradually, and cannot determine a date for repayment in the shortest possible time. Although Yang Zhiting, who was appointed by the Provincial Education Department, is still in Suzhou, he has not made a responsible statement. The forty-odd principals of the city then resolved at a meeting on the evening of the 21st to resign en masse and return all appointment letters to the County Education Bureau, requesting that personnel be dispatched to take over each school immediately. At this point, the schools in Suzhou are completely in a state of anarchy. The outgoing principals' association held another meeting yesterday morning and resolved: (1) To issue a declaration to the public, explaining the difficulties of not being able to maintain the situation any longer, (2) To send telegrams to the provincial authorities to report the situation. The current Education Bureau has also telegraphed the provincial authorities to ask for instructions on how to handle the situation. However, after this trend expanded, both sides are moving to extremes, and it may be difficult to resolve the situation in the short term. Ten thousand students will be deprived of education, and the problem of students graduating in the summer will be affected.

Educational Institutions to Adopt Uniform Official Document Format

In order to reform the format of official documents, the Ministry of Education has formulated a set of measures for a uniform format of official documents for educational institutions (the document is lengthy, but the main points are to eliminate various conventional clichés in official documents, use new-style punctuation, and simplify the process). The Ministry of Education itself has implemented this since May 1st. Now, it has issued this set of measures to the educational administrative organs of all provinces and cities, instructing them to uniformly implement it starting from July 1st. The order reads: "The measures for a uniform format of official documents for educational institutions have been formulated by the Ministry and issued to the Shanghai China Book Company for publication and distribution. They should be implemented according to a set schedule. It is hereby determined that July 1st of this year will be the date for the implementation of these measures. All official documents exchanged by educational institutions from that date onwards shall be handled in accordance with these measures. In addition to separate orders, a copy of the measures and five special discount coupons are enclosed herewith. You are hereby ordered to comply and to instruct your subordinates to comply with these measures." This order.

Free Talk

A Thought · Autumn · Water

Even if a man has sincerely given the key to his heart to a woman and married her, he still hopes that after she opens the door to his heart, she will not shut it carelessly.

There are some husbands who are like certain old-fashioned ornaments: too precious to discard, but useless to keep. Women don't know how to dispose of them, so they simply put them back on. This is not because of their inherent value, but because of the deep affection they once felt for them.

The field of love is like a battlefield, and its changes are even more dramatic. When a man swears he never wants to see her again and returns home late at night, feeling lost, he understands it in his heart and falls soundly asleep. But when he wakes up the next morning, he wonders why she hasn't called to check on him.

Men are often so contradictory. Ten minutes ago, he swore he would never have anything to do with another woman, but ten minutes later, he pities himself, feeling the loneliness of being single. A man in love cannot eat, sleep, or work unless he suddenly realizes one morning that he is already in love with a woman and decides to abandon his pursuit of her.

A woman's character can be considered the gentlest in the world. But when she hears that her old love is unhappy after marrying, she cannot help but feel a little bit of satisfaction and pride in her heart.

Gu Heyi · Awakening · Bewilderment

Wu-men's Gu Heyi passed away on the 17th of this month. Heyi can be considered a great painter of our time. Among painters, we lost Wu Guandai last year, and now we have lost Gu Heyi. The bad news arrived, and I cannot help but sigh. I have written a small biography to publish in this column.

Heyi's surname is Gu, his given name is Linshi, his style name is Xijin, and Heyi is his alias. He was from Wu-men. The Yuan Dynasty painter Huang Zijiu had the alias Yifeng Shanren. Heyi adopted this story and took the alias Yifeng Tingzhang. His paintings did not have a specific teacher but were able to reach the pinnacle of artistry because of his family's rich collection and his deep dedication to copying. The Gu family was a prominent clan in Wu-zhong. Gu Zishan, a prominent gentleman of Wu-men, was his grandfather. Zishan was wealthy and had a great love for bronze inscriptions, calligraphy, and painting. His collection was unmatched in his time. He had as many as ten thousand fans with calligraphy and paintings by famous artists, which he stored in the Wan-shan Lou. Other items can also be imagined. Zishan also enjoyed hosting guests. He built the Yi Garden on the old site of Wu Bao'an's residence in the Hulong Street of Chang-men, inviting prominent officials and dignitaries to evaluate bronze inscriptions, calligraphy, and painting. At that time, great experts in bronze inscriptions, such as Wu Qingqing, and great calligraphers and painters, such as Wu Changshuo and Lu Lianfu, often lingered there, using the Yi Garden as a place to evaluate bronze inscriptions, calligraphy, and painting. As a result, Zishan's collection of bronze inscriptions, calligraphy, and painting was not only the richest of the time but also the most exquisite. When calligraphers and painters from various places came to Wu-men, Zishan would invite them to stay at the Yi Garden. Modern painters such as Gu Ruobo, Hu Sanqiao, Wu Qiunong, Ni Mogeng, and the Zhu Ren from Shanyin were all guests of the Yi Garden at that time. Heyi was friends with various contemporary painters, learning from each other, and he also took previous generations of painters as his teachers, constantly studying their works. Therefore, his paintings did not have a specific teacher, but he was able to understand the principles of painting in his heart and grasp the deepest mysteries. In the past, Wu Yushan obtained a painting by Huang Zijiu and treated it as his teacher, eventually becoming a great master of the early Qing Dynasty. Heyi's family collection of paintings included works from the Song and Yuan dynasties, with nothing lacking and everything exquisite. It is no wonder that he became a great painter of our time. Heyi's paintings were once as famous as Lu Lianfu's. Lianfu excelled in landscapes, flowers, figures, and ladies, especially landscapes and flowers. Heyi specialized in landscapes. Commentators said that Lianfu's flowers truly captured the essence of the Nan-tian School, unmatched at the time. Heyi's landscapes were a true transmission of the Southern Song Dynasty, also unmatched. From what I have seen of Heyi's paintings, his imitations of the various masters of the Song and Yuan dynasties all captured their spirit. He was truly a great painter. Lianfu passed away many years ago, and now Heyi has also departed. It is truly a pity.

Garbage Island · Ji · Jin

South of the Mississippi River in New York, there is a small island, about dozens of miles in area, called Chuckras. According to legend, it was formed by the accumulation of garbage. Because the river is wide and both banks are prosperous areas of New York City, the amount of garbage dumped into it each year reaches more than 14,000 tons. From 1891 to the present, it has gradually emerged from the water as layers accumulate and overlap. Grass and trees grow on it, and animals live on it, almost no different from ordinary islands. Those who see it cannot help but marvel.

The formation of the island is mostly due to major geographical changes, such as erosion by seawater or the rising and falling of land. There has never been one formed by artificial construction. Even coral, which is good at living on the seabed, carrying sand and transporting soil, gradually rises to become an island. This exists in the South Pacific, but it is rare. Although this island is not very large, it has been increasing in area over the years. It is said that it can be connected to the mainland, and the soil is fertile and rich in sulfur and saltpeter, making it easy to grow things. This also shows that there is no waste in the world and the land has surplus benefits.

The Hospital Poisoning Case Within a Case · Bi · Ren

Recently, a case of a hospital maid being poisoned to death has been widely reported in Guangzhou. The matter is quite bizarre and has attracted the attention of the authorities. There is a person from Shunde named Huang Mengyi who runs the Qingchun Hospital at No. 47 Guangda Road, practicing Western medicine. He only provides outpatient services and does not have inpatient care. The family consists of Huang, his wife Ms. Feng, and three maids.

On the 2nd of this month, the maid A'er suddenly collapsed in the kitchen after breakfast. Her face was pale, and she was vomiting blood. Her breathing stopped. Huang suspected poisoning and began investigating. The residence is about seven or eight zhang deep and connects to Renkui Fang in the back. There is an open space under construction on the left, and the windows are often open, secured with iron bars. Huang and his wife live in the third room, while the maids live in the last room. Later, water stains were found on the pillows in Huang's room, as if they had been shot in from outside the window. The pillows were boiled and tested, and they were found to contain a highly poisonous substance called hydrocyanic acid.

After the incident, Huang was summoned to the Public Security Bureau. Under questioning, Huang stated that he had no enemies. However, there was one suspicious incident. Before the case occurred, at 12:00 AM and 3:00 AM the night before, someone knocked on the door repeatedly, asking for emergency treatment. When asked who had recommended them, what the symptoms were, and what the address was, they were evasive. Huang refused them. The next morning, the case occurred.

The poisoned maid was 23 years old and had some beauty but was not married. She had worked for Huang for seven or eight years and was usually very careful. It is a pity that she was suddenly poisoned. It is reported that a cat in the hospital also died suddenly a few days ago. The authorities believe that the matter is bizarre and that there is a case within a case, so they have ordered the police to investigate thoroughly.

Daqian's Exhibition Commemorating the Laying Down of His Brush · He · Tian · Jian

Today, there are two Zhangs in Shanghai, no less than the two Lus in Luoyang in the past. Their talent is timeless, and their brilliance reflects each other. This is a grand event in the art world. Shanzai is known as the Tiger Madman because he is good at painting tigers. In fact, he is proficient in landscapes, figures, and flowers and insects. Daqian has the reputation of being Shitao reborn. Once he puts down his brush, the wind and thunder accompany him. Only Shitao is worthy of comparison. Is it Shitao or Daqian? It is difficult to distinguish. Why is Daqian known for laying down his brush today? There is a reason for this. Since Daqian made his name with calligraphy and painting, there has been almost no day without people coming to his door seeking his work. The saying that "the threshold is worn through" is no exaggeration. However, Daqian is naturally unrestrained and does not adhere to conventions. He paints whenever he is in the mood. Those who seek his work often limit him by size and format. Daqian finds this very difficult. Sometimes he wants to create a large painting but is forced to make it small, and sometimes he wants to create a small painting but is forced to make it large. Size is not enough to restrain him, and the accumulation of painting debts has killed his interest. Therefore, Daqian often says to me, "What is a great man incapable of doing? Must I be enslaved by brush and ink?" He has wanted to lay down his brush many times. Last year, Daqian traveled east by sea, going to Shenyang, Dalian, Korea, and Beiping before returning. There were already hundreds of requests for paintings in his home. Fortunately, the mountains and rivers were before his eyes, the wind and clouds were under his wrist, and nature provided the drafts. His inspiration was abundant. He managed to offset the painting debts accumulated over the year. So he declared, "How can I bear to be a slave to paper and brush?" The act of laying down his brush was realized. His teacher, Zeng Nongran, heard about it and said to him, "Your name is already established. Once you lay down your brush, there must be a commemoration." Hence, there was the exhibition commemorating the laying down of his brush. When I heard about it, I said with emotion, "The world is suffering because it cannot gain fame, but Daqian, having already gained fame, looks away and abandons it. What will Daqian do? Being a slave to paper and ink is not the business of a man. However, Daqian's contempt for fame and fortune is beyond the reach of ordinary people." It is reported that the exhibition is held at the Ningbo Fellow Association. There are more than a hundred pieces on display. The collaborative fan paintings and twelve golden hairpins made by Shanzai and Daqian are also on display. The exhibition begins on the 21st. Since the beginning of the history of our art world, there have been few instances of someone becoming famous and then leaving. Daqian's actions are unprecedented. How can we not commemorate it? Therefore, I have written this article to record it.

A Western Beauty with Bobbed Hair and Cheongsam · Lu · Bing

The other day, I went from Xiaguan into the city for business and saw two rickshaws speeding towards me at the intersection of Banbian Street. I stood on the side of the road to wait for them to pass. I then saw that the passengers were not Chinese but Western women. One of the women was about forty years old, with a kind face, like a missionary. What was different was that her hair was tied in a bun, and she was wearing a gray silk cheongsam with a dark skirt. At first glance, it was difficult to tell. But her facial features and skin color revealed that she was a foreigner. I asked a friend about it, and he said that people in Beijing knew her quite well. She had been in China for more than ten years, and she was a senior female pastor. She could speak fluent Chinese and liked the comfort of Chinese clothing, so she was often seen not wearing Western clothes. According to my friend, near Xuanwu Lake and Qingliang Mountain, many Western young women who like to stroll around can be seen. Their eyes are blue, and their skin is fair. They imitate the current fashion, with bobbed hair and cheongsams, and their styles are graceful and charming. Some people look at them with the same gaze as Liu Zhen, and they are also generous and have no shyness. It is rumored that many of the Western women wearing Chinese clothes are family members of students studying abroad. They are stationed in the capital, so they accompany their husbands here. Having lived in China for a long time, they have been influenced by what they have seen and heard, and they have become Sinicized. This is not surprising. However, Western women who travel to China do have a growing tendency to like Chinese women's clothing. I have recorded this as a temporary anecdote.

Other Records of Hongdu · Xu · Chengyu

Each province has its own local taboo. People from Jiangxi are called "old acquaintances," while the name "wax chicken" is even older. During the Ming Dynasty, Li Shi once teased Xia Guixi with "Wax chicken alone has the taste of Jiangxi." Guixi immediately responded with "Horse bandits can empty the Hebei crowd." Li was from Beiping, and horse bandits were the local taboo there. When Yan Fenyi was in power, his fellow villagers went to congratulate him on his birthday. Fenyi was tall and imposing, and he stood tall. The people bowed and paid their respects. Gao Zhongxuan glanced sideways and laughed. Fenyi asked why. Zhongxuan said, "I just remembered Han Changli's poem, 'The big rooster comes proudly, and the little rooster waits respectfully,' which made me laugh." The crowd also laughed loudly. However, the origin of the colloquialism is unknown. A man from Jiangxi wrote a lantern poem on the Lantern Festival, saying: "Tassels are colorful and dazzling, and people come to see the lanterns on the thirteenth. Villagers meet and ask each other, why is our hometown called wax chicken?"

Jiangxi has a custom of renting wives. Wealthy families who have no sons often rent a fertile woman from poor families for a period of time. They pay according to the time. When the time comes, regardless of whether a son is born, she returns to her husband without any reluctance. Sometimes, the period is until a son is born. As soon as a son is born, she leaves. Sometimes, poor people have no way to make a living, so they lead their wives to seek rentals from wealthy families. Or, due to debt, they even have their wives go to the creditors. They return when the period is up. In recent years, although provinces and counties have strictly prohibited this, it has not been completely eradicated in remote areas.

Warmth in My Heart (One) (Nine) (Eight) · Bao · Tian · Xiao

Chapter Eleven: Emerald Garland, Pearl Hairpin, Beautiful Woman Returns, Scholar's Green Chamber, Crimson Tent, Famous Courtesan Marries Prominent Family

Originally, it is common to catch a cold and cough. There is nothing strange about it. Coughing can be very severe due to catching a cold, and it will get better after a while. However, Liu Xing-shu's cough is an incomplete cough, just a light and casual cough. It is commonly called a "half-sound cough." That kind of cough is a symptom of lung disease. It must be that there is something wrong with his lungs, and then this cough sound is produced. His lungs feel a little itchy or furry, and then he makes this cough sound in his throat. He often doesn't notice it himself, but others hear it very clearly. Zuo Shi-chen sees that Liu Xing-shu's cheeks are flushed, and he thinks that Xing-shu's lung disease is very deep, perhaps already in the second or third stage. However, he still goes to the bookstore every day and to the newspaper office every day, never missing a day of class. Zuo Shi-chen doesn't know what to say, but he advises him to take care of his body and to rest when he can. There is an old saying: "As long as the green hills remain, there will always be firewood to burn." It is harmful to the body to overwork. Liu Xing-shu said, "I am very grateful for your words. I also want to rest, but my circumstances do not allow me to rest. There is nothing I can do about it." After a pause, he said, "I think a person is cheap. One year, I didn't work for three months, just casually read a book, and I became decadent. At that time, my body felt lazy and dull, and it wasn't any better than now. Now, from morning till night, I don't have a moment of free time, and the days pass like this. Some people say that a person's brain is like a machine, it needs to be running every day. If it is abandoned and not used, the brain will rust like a machine." He smiled and said to Zuo Shi-chen, "I have translated ninety percent of my detective novel. In ten more days, I can finish it. This thousand dollars is unexpected, it came from out of the blue. Although I have stayed up so many nights, it is earned by my own hard work, like a craftsman making something. I seem to be very proud of myself." "I have already decided how to use this thousand dollars. This was not in the budget. I want to use it all to buy some jewelry. All young women like jewelry as decorations. This is also a natural and common thing. Moreover, their family's daughter, although she can't be said to be dripping with jewels, must have a few decent decorations. Marrying a wife now is different from before. Before, you married a wife and hid her at home, and she would never show her face or be seen by others. Now that is not possible. People often invite the wife along with the husband to parties. You have to take your wife with you. There are so many wives competing there. The beautiful wife attracts everyone's attention, as if the husband is glorified. The not-so-beautiful wife is, frankly speaking, overshadowed."
