The Elusive Gold Market

Fluctuations Remain Large ·· Result: Drop of 1.6 Taels

Silver Tax Issue Unresolved. Yesterday's gold market was still in a state of chaotic uncertainty, advancing and retreating, making it difficult to predict. The morning market was turbulent, with a change of as much as nine taels. The afternoon market calmed down slightly, with a difference of only a few cents per tael, but the trend was downward. The foreign exchange rate was reduced by half a point, but internally it seemed loose, with banks continuing to sell. Trading among firms varied, with Zhi Feng Yong, Fu Chang, Shun Li, and Wan Xing selling, while Yuan Mao Yong and hedging firms were buying. However, the psychology of all firms remained apprehensive and uneasy. From the early morning, there was a large-scale pullback, and due to the silver tax case not having any developments, the market opened high. Afterwards, sellers were very active, gradually moving downstream, rapidly falling to a low peak, plummeting by a large margin of eight or nine taels. This was due to the situation where exchange rates were effectively being loosened covertly. From 524 taels, it suddenly fell to within 516 taels, and then buyers rushed in, immediately pushing it back up three or four taels. However, the environment was confusing, and weakness reappeared. In the afternoon market, Heng Xing and Sheng Da sold, while buyers were scattered, and the market stabilized, with fluctuations only amounting to a few cents per tael. Later, it hovered around 517 taels.

The market opened with a jump of 3.5 taels. British silver fell by 3/16, while silver prices only decreased by 1/8. The opening price for July futures was 522 taels, an increase of 3.5 taels. The gross market initially strengthened but then weakened, retreating from 24.5 taels to around 21 taels. Initial notices were posted, with reductions of 1.25 for foreign exchange, 2.5 jiao for US dollars, and an increase of 0.625 for Japanese silver, then at 21.3 taels, which then decreased to 20.8 taels. Internal exchange rates remained stable. June's interbank trading was at 9 pence 8125, which increased to 22.1 taels after a few minutes, then suddenly weakened. Large firms leaned towards selling, mainly because exchange rates had loosened. June's interbank trading was at 9 pence 9375, and Japanese silver could be settled at 1.11375 taels, and the gold market seemed to be declining rapidly, plunging by six taels. At 10:30, it was only at 15.5 taels, then firms rushed to buy, jumping up four taels in just over twenty minutes, reaching 19.34 taels at 11:00. At noon, the downward trend returned, and sellers were tireless, reaching 17.2 taels at noon. After the market closed, it fell slightly more than one tael, which was quite chaotic and difficult to predict.

The afternoon market gradually became sluggish. The afternoon market opened with a drop of 1 tael and zero cents, at 516 taels, followed by 15.3 taels, due to the lower opening of goods. Shortly after, it gradually rose by more than two taels, reaching 17.89 taels at 2:45, with some buying activity. Mitsui bought nearby Japanese silver futures at 1.116875 taels, while British silver futures were traded nearby at 9 pence 875. Afterwards, it suddenly became sluggish, as sellers appeared strong on the trading floor. HSBC sold September British silver futures at 10 pence 125, and June Japanese silver futures were settled at 1.11625 taels, resulting in a drop of one or two taels. However, there were fluctuations of around one tael. At 4:00, it was at 16.12 taels, and then Wan Xing, Shun Li, and others bought in, returning to a high of over one tael, at 17.8 taels. However, hedging papers were being sold, so it was difficult to gain a foothold, and it fell to 16.5 taels, and finally to 17.1 taels. At the closing time of 4:30, it was at 16.9 taels, continuing to fall by 1.6 taels compared to the previous day. The maximum price in both the morning and afternoon markets was 24.5 taels, and the minimum price was 15.3 taels, a difference of 9.2 taels. Looking back, it had already been changed to 544.8 taels, reduced by 27 taels, and later reduced by 21 taels. Adding the ledger registration fee was a total of 17 taels. Goods opened at 23.5 taels in the morning, closed at 16.4 taels at noon, and 15.9 taels in the afternoon, with a closing price of 16.2 taels.

Different Intentions Among Traders. Transactions by various firms included Zhi Feng Yong, Fu Chang, Yuan Sheng, Yuan Da, Yuan Cheng Yong, and Yuan Yu Yong, who all sold. Da De Cheng, Yang Chang, Yu Da, and Fu Xing Yong traded with inconsistent movements. Shun Li and Wan Xing sold more than they bought. Cotton Market Downtrend Difficult to Reverse

Yesterday, telegraphs from the US regarding cotton showed mixed ups and downs. The local cotton market was soft and unremarkable. Japanese merchants were delivering this month's goods, and recipients were lacking, so the situation became more illusory, and the downtrend intensified. However, the Hubei gang and retail investors held on to distant futures, refusing to loosen. However, a certain manufacturer continued to sell short for October, and the number of bales was quite large. The current cotton business was quite quiet.

The Market Was Flooded with Recent Deliveries of Hubei Cotton The morning market opened with a strong position due to buyers holding tight. However, those delivering this month's goods flooded the market, falling by 5 cents, and distant months rose by 1 cent. In the afternoon, the market atmosphere suddenly loosened, and buyers were lacking, falling by 5 cents to 1 cent. The total transaction volume for the day was 27,500 dan. US Cotton: Old Rose, New Fell Yesterday, US cotton initially weakened due to a lack of major buyers and good weather, but then strengthened again due to purchases by peers, with old cotton rising by 5-7 pound-notes, new cotton falling by 6-7 pound-notes, and spot goods rising by 10 pound-notes. British cotton futures rose by 3-7 points, and spot goods rose by 5 points. Egyptian cotton spot goods fell by 5 points, and Indian cotton was closed. Silk, Tea: New Cocoons from Wujin and West Town Have Entered the Market

In various cities and towns of Wujin, there has been unrest this year, and farmers have been hesitant to raise silkworms in spring. The cocoon affairs in the west town are even worse than in the east town. Furthermore, due to unfavorable weather, both early and late cocoons have been affected. New cocoons from the west town have entered the market, and those from the east town have also begun clustering. Cocoon merchants in areas such as Lucheng, Sanhekou, Houyu, Menghe, and Benniu will set the scales today. New cocoons from the east town will also be seen in 24-25 days. Cocoon prices are expected to be as high as 60 yuan, with slight increases for improved varieties of high-quality cocoons. It is estimated that the cocoon production in Wujin this year will be at most 40-50% of the usual level.

The "Raise High, Lower Low" Tea Market of Foreign Firms

Qi Tea Rose Sharply to "Nian Liang" ·· Over 2,700 Chests Traded Yesterday, in the local tea market of foreign firms, British firms such as Jardine Matheson, Union Insurance, Tianyu, and Jinlong were increasingly eager to buy high-end Keemun black teas. Nearly all arriving goods were quickly sold, and the market situation was trending upwards. The total trading volume for the city reached 2,747 chests, and the market price opened at 225 taels, with the average price rising by another 20-30 taels compared to the previous day. However, foreign tea merchants rarely inquired about low-end black teas such as those from Wenzhou and He Kou, as well as green teas from local tea growers. The tea market of "raising high and lowering low" has become a natural trend, it is said.

The Market Price of Qi Floating "Three Character" Tea Is Plummeting

Keemun floating black tea, the top two grades have been purchased by various firms and there are no concerns about unsold goods. The third grade tea mountain households are also preparing batches for sale, but tea firms lack cash and cannot purchase in large quantities. Since the tea money robbery case in Liukou, many have been afraid to go to Jingdezhen to purchase tea. Most firms that have not arrived at the He Kou tea office have temporarily closed their warehouses, and tea sales have therefore been reduced and stagnant. In addition, the price of rice in Keemun has skyrocketed, at four and a half sheng per yuan. Workers at various tea firms are struggling to feed themselves, so they have shortened their periods and focused on purchasing fewer goods. Recently, the market price of Keemun floating "three character" black tea has fallen by 20 yuan, and few people are inquiring about it. The future of the tea market seems bleak, it is said.

Grain and Rice Market Sales Become Slightly More Active

Fresh Goods Are the Firmest

Yesterday, there were fewer than ten boats arriving at the Zhabei dock, and market sales became more active. As the weather cleared up slightly, various stores urgently needed to purchase small amounts. The demand for northern japonica rice was strong, but only fresh japonica rice was desirable. Prices rose slightly, but there was nothing noteworthy about old rice. Thin rice was scarce and only a small amount was available, with top-grade rice reaching 20 yuan in Guanwai. The sheep du and pointed foot variety was extremely firm, and although transactions were rare, the market was stable. The sales of high-grade "Tongbian" rice were slightly better, while mid-range rice was still sluggish, so the price fluctuated by one yuan, with high-grade at 18.5 yuan and mid-range falling by one yuan. The only movement in sales throughout the day was from customer gangs, so the market lacked ups and downs.

Shipments arriving at the Shanghai South River were not strong, and sales in the main street were inconsistent. Some "Xibei" japonica rice was already priced above 20 yuan, but most transactions were only for goods priced at 19.67 yuan, and the market was slightly firmer than the previous day. The sales of "Su Tong Ji" japonica rice were average. The "Tongchong" gang had slight expectations due to transportation issues, so sales were only moved marginally. The high-grade price was around 18 yuan. The early thin rice varieties such as "Lian Tang" and "Qing Jiao" from the South gang were also scarce here, and both supply and demand were low, so buyers raised prices, with行情帶緊 about half a角. Goods such as sheep tips were appearing and disappearing, with few transactions. The market shape was still uncertain, and the "變陰元" remained mediocre, with customer gang purchases quiet and prices unchanged, opening high around 18 yuan.

Flour Market Rise Moderates

Short Positions Have Been Covered ·· Momentum Is Difficult to Regain

Yesterday, the flour market presented a hovering appearance. Since the sharp rise this month, most of the non-industry shorts have gradually painfully covered their positions, and the target of those squeezing shorts has therefore relaxed slightly. In terms of customer sales, although Tianjin quotes were still around 3.78 yuan, current Shanghai flour was no longer worthwhile, so although inventories were low, demand was not very urgent. The situation in distant months, especially June, was still tight, as manufacturers feared they would have to continue to hold firm as half of the batch would be old flour, and the market in the future, was feared not to be able to convert small in the short term. By July, it would all be new flour, and if the wheat harvest was fruitful, manufacturers would no longer be able to hold firm, as their planning for the year could no longer use strategies that were suicidal. As a result, this month was slightly better than the previous day by 0.0025 yuan, June was unchanged, July was down 0.005 yuan, August was down 0.0025 yuan, September was up 0.005 yuan, and October was up 0.0025 yuan, it is said.

Local News

Grain Commission

Please Exempt Rice Tax First

Resolution of the Standing Committee Meeting

The Shanghai Grain Commission held its fifteenth standing committee meeting the other day. Xu Shuji, Huang Gutong, and commissioners from various bureaus and industries attended. Feng Liutang proposed that the price of rice is high and the people's food is difficult to obtain, and that various taxes on rice should be exempted to provide relief. It was considered that the price of rice is expensive, and the government should be requested to exempt taxes to protect the people's food. Moreover, checkpoints along the way often require tickets, which hinder transportation and cause great harm. After discussion, everyone agreed that the government has already made a determination to abolish the tax, and it is scheduled to be implemented on October 10th. At this time of high grain prices, the advance exemption of rice tax has limited losses and great benefits. It was resolved to submit a request for instructions. Furthermore, in view of the abundance of foreign rice, if no attention is paid to this year's rice crop, the future food shortage will be even more worrying. The various committees of the association also plan to submit their opinions to the municipal government for review.

Legitimate Aspirations of Chinese People

Letter from the Chinese Taxpayers' Association to Mr. Feitang

The Shanghai Chinese Taxpayers' Association sent a letter to Mr. Feitang, consultant of the Public Works Bureau, yesterday. The letter is quoted below: "To the esteemed Mr. Feitang, Our association sent letters to various organizations on April 9th to solicit opinions on the Shanghai issue. Now, the received replies are attached for your review. The opinions expressed in the letters are all legitimate aspirations of the Chinese people and should be adopted as much as possible. If there are other replies in the future, they will continue to be sent."

Shipping Industry

Studying the Sino-Japanese Agreement

Request to Announce the Negotiating Policy

After the Sino-Japanese treaty was signed by Foreign Minister Wang Rutang, although the Legislative Yuan was somewhat dissatisfied and raised questions, the storm quickly subsided after the Foreign Minister's personal explanation. Yesterday, the Shanghai Shipping Association and the Chinese Merchant Mariners Association, two groups, expressed doubts about the content of the new treaty. They submitted a request to announce the future negotiating policy of the shipping treaty, with many warnings. The document states: "Since the Daoguang and Xianfeng periods of the late Qing Dynasty, our country has repeatedly been forced to sign treaties that humiliate the country and infringe upon its rights. In addition to ceding land and paying indemnities, national taxes have been restricted, and foreign ships have been allowed to navigate inland. Even the tonnage tax on merchant ships has been unified. As a result, various countries have relied on this talisman, with their strong economies and surplus commodities, to compete with our country. Our country's industry and commerce, from the beginning to the present, have not escaped the status of handicrafts and small-scale machine industry. How can they compete with advanced countries? Therefore, foreign goods are becoming more and more abundant, and the hope for the development of domestic industry and commerce is becoming less and less. If industry and commerce are not developed, how can shipping be revitalized? Moreover, since the foreign goods of various countries are selling well, their economic power is becoming more inflated. Therefore, they have turned their attention to competition in the shipping industry, such as building new ships, reducing transportation costs, and engaging in competition in every way. Our government has no tax laws to protect merchants, and the ports are wide open. The economy and ships of the Chinese people are insufficient. Even if they want to compete, it is difficult to do so. The situation has already been formed, and even a great sage can do nothing. Alas, the Chinese people have been bound and moaning, exploited and oppressed, by such unequal treaties for more than eighty years. Anyone with a little knowledge and a little blood will be heartbroken and sigh with regret, vowing to make up for it. Does not the late Premier, on the verge of death, repeatedly and earnestly exhort us to abolish unequal treaties as his legacy? His sincerity is enough to move gods and open metal and stone. Our association and others either engage in shipping as merchants or rely on navigation as their sole means of livelihood. We earnestly hope that the late Premier's legacy will be realized. How so? If these unequal treaties are not fundamentally abolished for one day, and coastal navigation rights are not actually recovered for one day, then our country's shipping industry will have no reason to develop for one day, and our association and others will be in deep despair for one day. Although our association and others consider themselves insignificant, we can say that we have thought deeply and planned carefully about this issue of our own survival and extinction. What we cannot do is that the merchant ships of various countries have penetrated deep into our hinterland and are flooding the coast. It is as if they have seized our throat and poisoned our brains. Even if we want to rise up and fight, we cannot. Fortunately, the Japanese treaty has expired, which is the only opportunity to correct the humiliation and loss of rights. Therefore, our association and others do not hesitate to appeal to our government to take care of the remaining vitality of the shipping industry, and strive to actually recover coastal navigation rights when signing the commercial treaty this time, so that shipping merchants will not go bankrupt and sailors will not lose their jobs. We have not yet received a clear indication. Upon reading the full text of the Sino-Japanese Customs Agreement signed on the 6th of this month, although the navigation treaty has not been agreed upon, the second article states that "the treatment given to the government or its people of that country in respect of ship taxes and all matters related to the above, shall not be less favorable than the treatment now or in the future given to its own people or any other foreign government and its people. Also, ships of China or Japan shall, within the territory of the other country, receive treatment in respect of ship taxes and all matters relating to ship taxes not less favorable than that now or in the future received by ships of any other country." This is tantamount to implicitly permitting Japanese ships to continue to have the right to sail and carry goods in our country's coastal and inland waters in the future. The efforts of the people to abolish the unequal treaties are still as they were. Then what hope do our associations have? Although this does not include specific provisions for navigation, since there is a provision that is no less favorable than any other country now or in the future, then the existing treaties of various countries have not yet expired. Even if the treaty expires in the future, if any other country has an excuse not to abandon the navigation rights it has plundered, then we cannot treat Japan differently. With each other interacting in turn, is it not possible that navigation rights will never be recovered? However, our associations deeply hope that this view is inaccurate. Therefore, we venture to present this request to our wise diplomatic authorities, and clearly announce the policy for the future navigation treaty and the practical steps for recovering navigation rights. As the saying goes, "If you are prepared, you will have no worries." Since shipping is related to the circulation of goods, if navigation rights are recovered, and Japan cancels its ships in our coastal and Yangtze River waters, it will inevitably lead to fewer ships and more goods, and the stagnation of goods. How should our country increase ships, or how should we buy their ships and docks, etc.? There should be prior planning for everything, so that there will be no panic when the time comes. This really depends on the strategy and regulations of our government, and then merchants can easily arrange things. The opportunity is pressing, so why does the government still have no indication? Does the department only seek equality in the text of the treaty, and the mutual inland navigation is not mutually beneficial, and the responsibility for competition rests with the merchants? If so, then our associations dare to solemnly tell the diplomatic authorities who inherit the spirit of the late Premier's uncompromising spirit, that this is another suicidal treaty! The rate of progress of material civilization is like a parabola, accelerating downwards. Therefore, Japan can complete the restoration of the entire city of Tokyo in six and a half years, while our country may not be able to build a road in three years. There is no other reason, but industry, commerce, economy, science, and talent are all lagging behind. In fact, it is like this, but we still want to comfort ourselves with equality and reciprocity in the text. Is it reciprocity? Or is it unique? It is not up to the wise to decide. Try to be more practical. Japanese ships are said to be 5 million tons, while our country is less than 300,000 tons. The age of Japanese ships is mostly under 20 years, while our country's are over 30 years. One in a hundred of our ships go to Japan. Japanese ships import more than ours. In fact, it is like this, even if we want to comfort ourselves, can we? Therefore, if our diplomatic authorities conclude a treaty with Japan this time, if they do not observe the true situation of our country's shipping industry, and do not actually cancel Japan's right to navigate and carry goods in our coastal and inland waters, and only seek the splendor of the surface, it is the government's intention to abandon our sailors. Then our associations will have no choice but to stop working, stop shipping, and die in the East China Sea. How can we bear to still be trampled on and slaughtered under the clear sky and white sun? Everyone loves life, who is not like me? It is also shameful to live shamefully. Forced to this point, we make this cry of sorrow, and we only hope that our government will appreciate our foolish sincerity, forgive our excitement, and quickly announce the negotiating policy and the practical steps for recovering navigation rights, so as to comfort our expectations and facilitate preparations. The country is fortunate, and our associations are very fortunate.

Japanese Invasion of Navigation Rights

Preventing Chinese Ships from Going to Japan from Dalian

Shanghai Shipping Association Submits a Request to the Ministry to Argue

The Shanghai Shipping Association submitted a document to the Ministry of Communications yesterday, stating, "We are reporting the details of the Chinese ships in Dalian that did not load goods and went to Japan, and we ask for your review and implementation. According to the Ministry's Order No. 1616, it was stated that the Dalian Japanese Maritime Bureau prevented Chinese ships from loading goods to Japan in Dalian. The association previously sent a telegram on behalf of the company and has already telegraphed the Dalian Customs to earnestly negotiate and approve the record. Now, according to the Dalian Customs Commissioner, the Chinese ships left for Japan on May 10 without loading goods. The details have been informed to the Shanghai Shipping Association by Zhengji Company and forwarded to the Ministry, etc., according to this situation, it is appropriate to order to inform and report the details, etc., according to this order, the association previously received a report from member Zhengji Company, and received a telegram from Dalian, the Chinese ships of the Yingkou Overseas Trade Company, which represents the company, planned to load the goods scheduled to go to Japan in Dalian, but were suddenly stopped by the Dalian Japanese Maritime Bureau. Please report the matter to the association by telegram for negotiation, etc., according to the situation, the Ministry was informed by telegram, and the Dalian Customs was telegraphed to earnestly negotiate, etc., according to the record, Zhengji Company then sent a letter saying that the Chinese ships were prevented from loading goods in Dalian by the Japanese Maritime Bureau. Now, a letter from Dalian says, "The ship is scheduled to load a full ship of coal to Japan. The contract states that it will first be loaded in Yingkou to the extent that it can sail out (calculated to be 4,500 tons of coal loaded in Yingkou), and the remaining empty space will be added in Dalian (there is still 4,000 tons of empty space). According to the investigation, our ship used to load goods from Dalian to Japan, which is a normal thing, and there has never been any hindrance. Up to now, many Western ships have also transported goods from Dalian to Japan, and there has never been any hindrance. Unexpectedly, this time, the Chinese ships were actually prohibited from loading and transporting by the Dalian Maritime Bureau. According to the director of the bureau, Dalian is a Japanese port and foreign ships are not allowed to load goods to Japan, etc. However, foreign ships are not prohibited, and only our Chinese ships are discriminated against. After repeated negotiations, they were not allowed to accommodate. In this situation, if we wait for a long time, the loss will be huge. We were forced to abandon the 4,000 tons of empty space and sail to Yokohama. This move is not small for the loss of a Chinese ship and the future shipping relations of Chinese ships. Please ask the association to urge the department to seriously negotiate to maintain navigation rights, etc." According to the association's investigation, Dalian is our country's territory, and Japan is a friendly country. There is no precedent for prohibiting merchant ships from transporting goods. Now, the Japanese Maritime Bureau in the port suddenly prevented our country's merchant ships from transporting goods from Dalian to Japan, which is not only wantonly destroying our country's shipping industry, but is actually intentionally infringing on our country's sovereignty. The matter is of great importance and cannot be tolerated. We urge the department to consult with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to seriously negotiate to prevent aggression and protect sovereignty. We cannot wait."

President Tan

Urging Foreign Minister Wang to Return to Beijing After His Leave

Handwritten Letter Entrusted to Fan Guang to Deliver to Shanghai

After Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting came to Shanghai the other day, he took a leave of absence from the Executive Yuan for two weeks due to physical discomfort and recuperation at his Shanghai residence on Gubalu Road. He entrusted Counselor Fan Guang of the ministry to carry the documents to Beijing. After President Tan received the report, he believed that the ministry's affairs were busy and depended on him to preside over them, so he approved a leave of absence for one week and wrote a handwritten letter urging him to return to Beijing after his leave, entrusting Counselor Fan to deliver it to Shanghai. Mr. Fan came to Shanghai by car the night before and went to Mr. Wang's residence immediately after arriving at the North Station yesterday morning. It is reported that he presented President Tan's letter and told Mr. Wang about the eagerness of his colleagues in the ministry.

Chen Yi, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Military Affairs; Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Industry and Commerce; and Lin Sen, member of the Central Committee, all left Beijing together the night before and came to Shanghai by night train on the Beijing-Shanghai line, arriving in Shanghai yesterday morning.

Sends Personnel to Shanghai to Investigate Military Property

After the Ministry of Military Affairs of the National Government commissioned Hu Qin, the Director of Investigation, and committee members Chen Ruling, Xu Zhensheng, and Heidekui last year to investigate the military property of 22 counties in Jiangsu and Zhenjiang, they went to Jiangdu, Zhenjiang, and other counties for investigation. Yunnan Customs Changes Tax Collection Method

Yunnan Chamber of Commerce Cables Shanghai to Ask the Central Government to Postpone Implementation

Yunnan's finances are chaotic, and paper money is rampant. Each yuan of paper money is only worth 30% of the common silver dollar, but customs duties can be fully paid in paper money. It is now heard that Yunnan Province Customs has been ordered to increase cash collection, or to pay the actual price in paper money. Yunnan merchants and people have already had weak purchasing power and poor business due to chaotic finances. Now, the burden has suddenly increased, and it is impossible to pay for a while. A few days ago, the General Chamber of Commerce of Yunnan Province and other groups sent a telegram to the Yunnan Fellow Association in Shanghai, requesting the Central Government to temporarily postpone the implementation and temporarily stop redeeming goods. The telegram and the association's reply are recorded below:

Telegram from Yunnan Chamber of Commerce and various groups to Mr. Zhang Rongxi and other gentlemen of the Yunnan Fellow Association in Fanwang Palace: "The Yunnan Customs has increased the water content by 10 times, and the postage stamps have increased by 5 times. The Central Government originally decided to increase the collection after Yunnan's finances were restored. We have repeatedly telegraphed the Central Government to ask for consideration of the increasing chaos in Yunnan's finances and postpone the implementation, but we have not received a reply. The Customs authorities insist on implementation, resulting in imports and exports being suspended due to waiting for the reply. We urge you to ask the Central Government to immediately telegraph the Customs authorities to temporarily postpone the implementation to alleviate the people's difficulties and maintain the merchants' difficulties. We look forward to your reply. The Yunnan General Chamber of Commerce and various groups kowtow." The Yunnan Fellow Association in Shanghai replied to the Yunnan General Chamber of Commerce and various groups: "We have received your telegram and will follow your instructions to strive for the support of the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Transportation, and the Ministry of Industry. We hope that you will telegraph the Central Government again and ask the provincial government to strive for support. The Yunnan Fellow Association in Shanghai."

Supervision by the Municipal Supervisory Committee

Handling of Compensation for the May 30th Massacre

Letter Received from the Central Secretariat Yesterday

City Government to Collect and Forward

The issue of compensation for the families of those who died in the May 30th Massacre has been negotiated many times. The Public Concession eventually agreed to pay 150,000 yuan in compensation to be distributed to the families of the victims. However, the representatives of the May 30th Massacre Family Association, such as Hu Changsheng, did not follow proper procedures when distributing the compensation, resulting in the fraudulent receipt of compensation. As a result, Luo Chenshi and Luo Wenlin and others filed a lawsuit in court against Hu Changsheng and others, and Hu Changsheng sued Wang Zhaohua and others for embezzling compensation. The Standing Committee of the Central Party Headquarters was concerned about the dispute caused by this case and instructed the Municipal Party Supervisory Committee to supervise and handle it quickly. The original letter stated, "Recently, the Standing Committee issued a statement that the 150,000 yuan in compensation from the British Public Works Bureau for the May 30th Massacre should be collected and forwarded to the families of the deceased by the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, and the Municipal Supervisory Committee should be instructed to supervise the distribution and report it." After receiving the letter, the association resolved at the Fifth Standing Committee meeting yesterday (22nd) to appoint Comrade Zhu Yingpeng to handle the matter jointly with the municipal government.

Social Affairs Bureau

Promoting Domestic Goods with New Initiatives

Organizing Basic Production and Sales Cooperatives for Domestic Goods

Since the sharp decline in silver prices, the national economy has experienced extreme panic. Frugality to save the crisis has become the center of public opinion at the moment. Promoting domestic goods is the first priority in the cry for frugality. The Shanghai Municipal Council had a resolution to promote domestic goods by organizing basic family groups, which was handed over to the Social Affairs Bureau to formulate specific measures and report to the council for discussion. It is now heard that the Social Affairs Bureau has drafted a charter for the Basic Production and Sales Cooperatives for Domestic Goods, consisting of 20 articles, and submitted it to the municipal government for review and implementation. Because the charter is closely related to the future of the industry, it is specifically scheduled to be discussed in detail at 2:00 pm on the 29th of this month in the bureau to solicit public opinions for reference by the municipal government during the review. The original text of the document submitted by the Social Affairs Bureau to the municipal government and the draft charter are recorded below for those who are concerned about the people's livelihood.

Social Affairs Bureau Submits Document to the Municipal Government for Reporting

According to the Ministry's Order No. 3639, "It is hereby ordered that the proposal to promote domestic goods by organizing basic family groups has been resolved at the 151st Municipal Council meeting. "The Social Affairs Bureau shall formulate specific measures and report to the council for discussion, etc." The Social Affairs Bureau shall comply with this order immediately. I believe that it is difficult to develop based solely on the unity of consumers without considerable connection with the production side. Therefore, the basic family group is proposed as a group of consumers (referred to as Class A members), and domestic goods factories or sellers are a group of production suppliers (referred to as Class B members). There are two groups that are connected to each other, so it is difficult to name the charter. It is named the Basic Production and Sales Cooperative for Domestic Goods, which is still not satisfactory. The mutually beneficial relationship between the two groups is detailed in the section on the rights and obligations of Class A and Class B members of the charter. I believe that our country is a country with backward industry and commerce, and it is also a country that is most severely affected by foreign economic aggression. The power of foreign goods is overwhelming, and the people are accustomed to using them without discernment, which is not easy to correct. Moreover, domestic goods are not manufactured as well and are not sold as cheaply. Years of promotion have not been very effective. This is partly the reason. In order to encourage those who use domestic goods to participate enthusiastically, it seems appropriate to have considerable encouragement to arouse them. Therefore, it is stipulated that the products of Class B members must be purchased by Class A members, and they also have the right to enjoy special discounts. Class B members have this large group of customers and are supported by the government, such as free proof, free advertising, tax exemption inspection fee reduction, etc., so it should be reasonable for them to be happy to join the association. As for the progress of the association's affairs, it is planned to entrust the Domestic Goods Exhibition Hall under the jurisdiction of the bureau to preside over it to save expenses. The association's income will be used to develop the association's affairs. Due to the previous orders, we have drafted a draft charter for the Basic Production and Sales Cooperative for Domestic Goods, consisting of 20 articles, and respectfully submit it to your Excellency for review and guidance. It is for the public good."

Draft Articles of Association of the National Goods Production and Sales Cooperative

Article 1: This cooperative aims to revitalize the national goods industry and is named the Shanghai Special Municipality National Goods Production and Sales Cooperative. Article 2: This cooperative is composed of the following two types of members: (A) Basic Family Units (referred to as Class A members): all citizens of the Republic of China who pledge to use national goods belong to this category; (B) National Goods Production Units (referred to as Class B members): all citizens of the Republic of China who manufacture or sell national goods belong to this category. Article 3: Class A members must submit an application form and a pledge when joining the cooperative, along with two 2.5-inch half-length photos of themselves and their representative. Article 4:

Page 14

May 23, 1930, Republic of China (Shen Bao, Fourth Section), Friday (14)

Class A members shall fulfill the following obligations: 1. Abide by the pledge and follow all rules and regulations of the cooperative; 2. For products already produced by Class B members, refrain from purchasing other products; 3. Whenever national goods are applicable, refrain from using foreign goods; 4. Invest in the national goods industry to the best of their ability; 5. Strive to promote the national goods movement. Article 5: Class A members shall enjoy the following rights: 1. Purchase products from Class B members with preferential treatment compared to general buyers; 2. Have the right to request the cooperative to investigate or handle the procurement of national goods that are not available in the city; 3. Enjoy samples of new products from Class B members; 4. Enjoy the cooperative's publications and participate in exhibitions, tours, and other artistic events. Article 6: Class B members, when joining the cooperative, in addition to submitting an application form and pledge, must also provide the name and address of the factory or business location, the name of the manager, a catalog of products, the selling price, and preferential treatment measures for Class A members. Article 7: If there are any doubts about the qualifications of Class B members or their products, they may submit a request to the Social Affairs Bureau for verification. Article 8: Class B members must fulfill the following obligations: 1. When Class A members purchase goods, they must honestly fulfill the agreed-upon preferential treatment measures; 2. Refrain from passing off foreign goods as national goods or selling inferior goods to members; 3. Report new products to the cooperative in a timely manner so that members can be notified; 4. Strive to collect national goods to meet the needs of members; 5. The obligations of Class A members must also be followed. Article 9: Class B members shall enjoy the following rights: 1. Be entitled to request the Shanghai Special Municipality Social Affairs Bureau to certify their products as national goods free of charge; 2. Be exempt from advertising tax for legitimate national goods advertisements; 3. Be entitled to a reduction in inspection fees for national goods raw materials entrusted for industrial inspection; 4. Be able to request the cooperative to promote and introduce them when raising capital; 5. Be able to request the cooperative to distribute samples of new national goods on their behalf; 6. Be entitled to the cooperative's publishing rights. Article 10: If any member fails to comply with the pledge or regulations and is reported by other members with evidence, the committee shall impose sanctions as appropriate. The sanctions are of the following three types: 1. Warning; 2. If the warning is given twice and there is still no repentance, the membership may be suspended for one week to one month; 3. If, after the previous two types of sanctions, there is still no remorse, the matter may be brought before the general membership meeting for expulsion from the cooperative. Article 11: Members of the cooperative shall pay an annual membership fee of one yuan. The first year's membership fee shall be paid upon joining the cooperative. Failure to pay the membership fee shall be deemed as voluntary withdrawal from the cooperative. Article 12: All members of the cooperative shall be issued a membership card, which shall be renewed once a year. Article 13: In addition to recording the member's name and other information, the membership card shall also include the cooperative's regulations, the business location of Class B members, the product catalog, and preferential treatment measures. Article 14: The general membership meeting shall be held every six months and convened by the committee. Article 15: The committee shall consist of nine members, with four members each elected from Class A and Class B members by the general membership meeting, and the director of the National Goods Exhibition Hall of this municipality serving as an ex officio member. Article 16: The committee shall have three standing committee members, with the director of the National Goods Exhibition Hall serving as an ex officio member, and one member each elected from the members elected from Class A and Class B members to serve as standing committee members. Article 17: The committee shall hold a regular meeting once a month, and special meetings shall be held as needed, convened by the standing committee members when necessary. Article 18: All affairs of the cooperative shall be entrusted to the National Goods Exhibition Hall for handling. Article 19: The detailed rules for the cooperative's deliberation shall be established separately. Article 20: These articles of association shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Special Municipal Government.

Tax Exemption for National Goods Advertisements

The Provisional Measures Drafted by the Three Bureaus of Finance, Social Affairs, and Public Utilities Have Been Approved by the Municipal Government and Ordered to Be Implemented Immediately. The three bureaus of finance, social affairs, and public utilities of this municipality, regarding the tax exemption for national goods advertisements, previously resolved two measures at the 153rd Municipal Affairs Meeting: (A) Those who post advertisements on public advertisement sites built by the Municipal Government shall only pay rent, and the national goods advertisement tax shall be completely exempted; (B) The goods sold in the advertisement shall first submit certification documents from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce or the former Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce to the Social Affairs Bureau for inspection to confirm that they are indeed national goods before the above measures can be applied. The advertising management rules of this municipality should be reviewed and revised accordingly. However, before the revision, in order to facilitate implementation, several provisional measures have been specially drafted for compliance. If there are no obstacles during implementation in the future, the rules will be revised in accordance with these measures. It is reported that the provisional measures were approved by the Municipal Government yesterday and ordered to be implemented immediately. The articles are excerpted as follows: (1) Advertisements displaying the name and image of legitimate national goods, or the name of merchants solely manufacturing and selling legitimate national goods, shall be exempt from advertising tax; (2) Advertisements for legitimate national goods must first submit certification documents from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce or the former Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce and the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs to the Advertising Management Office of the Public Utilities Bureau for inspection to confirm that they are legitimate national goods before they can be exempted from tax; (3) A handling fee shall be charged for all legitimate national goods advertisements to subsidize expenses such as surveying, registration, stamping, and licensing. The amount shall be calculated at 20% of the tax rate for each type of advertisement as stipulated in the original Shanghai Municipal Advertising Management Rules, except for paper advertisements, which are subject to the original regulations; (4) Advertisements for national goods luxury goods and entertainment items shall be calculated at 80% of the original tax rate stipulated in the Shanghai Municipal Advertising Management Rules; (5) Temporary advertisements (i.e., paper advertisements) shall be charged a handling fee in accordance with the original regulations, and rent for public advertisement sites shall also be charged, with the amount calculated at 40% of the tax rate stipulated in the Shanghai Municipal Advertising Management Rules; (6) The procedures for posting tax-exempt advertisements shall still be handled in accordance with the provisions of the Shanghai Municipal Advertising Management Rules.

Order Issued by the Municipal Government

Regulations for the Management of Prepared Medicines

Separate Orders to the Three Bureaus of Public Safety, Health, and Social Affairs for Compliance The Municipal Government yesterday approved a consultation from the Ministry of Health, stating that prepared medicines are products that can be freely purchased and taken by the public without the instructions of a physician for the purpose of treating diseases. If the preparation is improper, the drawbacks are quite worrying. Moreover, there are a few unscrupulous merchants who only know how to profit and disregard the interests of others. The various prepared medicines they sell are either imported from abroad or deliberately fabricated, relying on false and exaggerated advertisements as a tool to promote sales, claiming that one medicine can cure hundreds of diseases, enticing people to buy and take them. Patients, greedy for convenience, lightly try them. Not only are the effects completely absent, but they are also sufficient to delay their treatment period. In the past, the government had no specific regulations for the management of these prepared medicines, nor any legal chemical testing. Therefore, whether the preparation method is appropriate, whether the raw materials are excellent, and whether the advertisements and leaflets have the disadvantages of exaggeration are all impossible to assess, which is not a serious way to treat people's lives. The Ministry, in view of this, has already drafted a draft of regulations for the management of prepared medicines and submitted it to the Executive Yuan for approval. In addition to separate consultations, a copy of the regulations for the management of prepared medicines is attached, hoping that they will be reviewed and ordered to be followed by the subordinate units. It is reported that the Municipal Government has instructed the three bureaus of public safety, health, and social affairs to follow the regulations accordingly.

Announcement by the Citizens Training Association

Procedures for Organizing Trade Unions

The procedures for organizing trade unions in Shanghai Special Municipality have been announced and implemented by the Citizens Training Association. The original text is as follows: (1) To initiate the organization of a trade union, there must be a joint signature of more than 50 workers who are 16 years of age or older and currently engaged in the same industry or the same occupation. Representatives should be elected to prepare a written explanation and a resume of the initiators (the resume form can be obtained from the Association), with one original and one copy, and apply to the Association for permission; (2) After accepting the application, the Association will immediately send personnel to inspect the main points: (1) Whether the submitted reasons are legitimate and accurate; (2) Whether the members are loyal; (3) Whether there is a trade union or similar organization in the industry; (4) What is the relationship with the employers; (5) Whether there is a need for organization; (3) After receiving the report from the inspectors, the Association will review and approve whether to allow the establishment and inform the Social Affairs Bureau for reference; (4) After the trade union receives the Association's approval to prepare for establishment, it should immediately send personnel to the Association to collect the license certificate; (5) The trade union that has been approved for preparation should elect preparatory members (the number of members is based on the general rules), organize a preparatory committee, and submit it to the Association and the Social Affairs Bureau for record. The Association may send personnel to guide it when necessary; (6) The preparatory committee should engrave the committee's seal according to the name approved by the Association. The shape is a square of 1.5 inches, with 2 points on each side. The text reads "Preparatory Committee of the XXX Association of Shanghai Special Municipality". The text should be in regular script, and the date of activation and the seal should be reported for record; (7) The preparation period for the trade union is limited to three weeks after the filing of the preparatory committee. After the preparation is completed, the draft articles of association and the membership list should be submitted to the Association for review (the paper for copying the articles of association and the membership list can be obtained from the Association); (8) The articles of association of the trade union should specify the following items: (A) Name; (B) Purpose; (C) Area and address; (D) Qualifications, rights and obligations of members; (E) Regulations on members' admission, withdrawal and expulsion; (F) Regulations on the number, powers and resignation of staff; (G) Regulations on meetings; (H) Regulations on membership fees and other accounting matters; (I) Regulations on mutual aid undertakings; (J) Regulations on amendment of the articles of association; (K) Regulations on dissolution and liquidation; (9) After the articles of association and the membership list of the trade union are approved by the Association, a founding meeting should be convened immediately and the Association should be requested to send personnel to guide it; (10) After the trade union is established, a list of important officers and a summary of the trade union (the forms can be obtained from the Association) should be filled out immediately, and the changes in the articles of association and the membership list should be stated and submitted to the Association. After the Association sends personnel to review it and considers it to be sound, the Association will issue an order to prove it and inform the Social Affairs Bureau for reference; (11) After receiving the above order, the trade union should immediately apply to the Social Affairs Bureau for registration; (12) If the union has any of the following circumstances, it should be submitted to the Association for approval and record at any time: (A) The date of convening the general membership meeting or the representative meeting; (B) Re-election of officers; (C) Admission and withdrawal of members; (D) Levy of special funds, temporary fundraising or shares; (E) Punishment or expulsion of members; (F) Reorganization or dissolution; (G) The result of applying to the court for bankruptcy and liquidation; (13) The organization procedures have been announced and implemented by the Association.

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau

Research on Raw Silk Grading Standards

Organize the Raw Silk Grading Committee

The Raw Silk Inspection Department of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau believes that the work of the department is not only limited to inspection but also to the research of raw silk quality so that the raw silk exported can be gradually improved and foreign trade developed. Therefore, it has specially formulated research work to be carried out step by step, and the plan is of particular importance. Because there is no unified grading standard for Chinese silk, and there are no regulations for each grade, the silk firms in Shanghai have to list the silk brands of various factories into several grades for the convenience of trade. However, this grading has no standard, and the manufacturers do not know which grade their products can be classified into. The brands at the top level are not necessarily perfect, and those at the lower level are not necessarily inferior. Medium-sized manufacturers know that their brands are not well-known, and even if they have good products, it is difficult to get a good price. The quality of goods is ignored. On the contrary, if Chinese raw silk has unified grades and each grade has a specified standard, American silk factories can choose a grade according to their needs, sign a contract to purchase, and manufacturers can produce according to their abilities. If they can improve the quality of goods, they can get a higher price. Therefore, in order to improve the quality of raw silk and facilitate foreign trade, it is urgent to stipulate raw silk grading standards. Now, in addition to hiring experts to be responsible for the work, the department has also sent letters to the Shanghai Silk Merchants Association and the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Silk Cocoon General Office to recommend personnel to jointly organize the Raw Silk Grading Committee to solve the grading problem. The procedure is: (1) Collect Chinese factory silk from the aspects of uniformity, cleanliness, cleanness, evenness, tensile strength, and other quality aspects to engage in testing. Send the test results to the Raw Silk Grading Committee for discussion, and the committee will formulate the grades and standards for each grade; (2) After the grade standards are formulated, the committee will report to the representative agencies for approval and submit them to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for record; (3) After the record is made, the selected grades and standards should be adopted as the Chinese raw silk grading standards in conjunction with the silk industry groups.

Central Bank Inspection Report

54th Time

The 54th Central Bank issuance reserve inspection report said that the Association is responsible for the issuance of banknotes in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Act, and is responsible for the inspection of the issuance of exchange coupons. The 54th inspection was held in the issuance bureau of the Bank on May 20, 1930, and the inspection results are announced as follows: the total amount of exchange coupons issued was 14,870,004 yuan in silver, including 13,718,711 yuan in silver coupons and 1,151,293 yuan in auxiliary currency coupons. The total amount of exchange coupon reserves was 14,870,004 yuan, including 9,946,999.2 yuan in cash reserves. The cash reserves were 6,188,178.31 yuan in the Bank's issuance treasury, 1,253,635.14 yuan in branch banks in various ports, and 2,500,5185.75 yuan in the same industry. The guaranteed reserves were converted into 4,923,004.8 yuan in silver. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank exchange coupon regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guaranteed reserve is 40%. The inspection results show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank of China on May 20, 1930, Li Fusun, Supervisors, Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilu,

Instructions on Investigating and Resolving Backlog Cases

Yuan Liang's Order to All Districts

The Shanghai Special Municipality Public Security Bureau instructed all districts to: for the matter of issuing a notice, the First Division presented a list of kidnapping cases in each district, which has been read. The responsibility of the police is to maintain public security and protect the lives and property of the people. This city is a mixed place with waterways in all directions, and it is adjacent to the concession, which is a hiding place for criminals. Therefore, major kidnapping cases occur from time to time. The residents of the whole territory are uneasy day and night, and they rely on strict arrests to ensure that all cases are solved and all criminals are punished, so that the law can establish its authority and the bandits can know to retreat. Since the director took office, he has been working hard on the arrest of criminals, and he has been sparing no effort. Whenever there is a major case solved, he has not been stingy with heavy rewards of thousands of gold and promotions beyond the grade. All requests from each district to add police and weapons, to the extent possible, are all approved immediately. In addition, detectives are assigned to facilitate command and given detective fees to facilitate activities. The salaries and allowances of the detectives are also increased, and they are given considerable power without any conditions. The intention is to encourage colleagues to be loyal and strive to achieve the goal of cleaning up the whole territory and making a pre-emptive move to recover the concession. Previously, due to the large number of backlog cases, repeated orders were issued to clear them up and resolve them within a time limit. After reviewing the list in detail, from February 27 to the 6th of this month, there are still more than 30 unsolved cases. The number of backlog cases in each district is as high as six, and as few as two, three, or four. It seems that such arbitrary delays are really unacceptable. The director of this bureau is in charge of the important task of introspection, and he cannot sleep well and eat well. The captains of the districts are responsible for their respective districts, but they are sitting idly by and allowing the stacking of cases, the swallowing of boats, the escape of criminals, and the looting of goods, and the victims are suing without a door. The salaries you receive are the people's wealth, and you do not feel guilty in the clear night. For this reason, a copy of the list is sent to all districts. The captains of each district should immediately check the cases in their respective districts on the list, urge their subordinates to strengthen the investigation and arrest within a time limit, and make sure to capture the real culprits and bring them to justice to quell the banditry and appease the people. The district chiefs should also be fully responsible for the cases in their respective districts and supervise the police officers and detectives to investigate and arrest them according to the severity of the cases, offer rewards to purchase information, divide the work and cooperate closely, and conduct strict investigation. The district officers, patrol officers, chiefs, and police officers have their own responsibilities and cannot shirk them. All detectives are especially responsible for their duties. Within one month, the district chiefs should find out the details of each case in their respective districts listed in the list, as well as kidnapping incidents that occur later, and report them with details of the investigation process, indicating whether they have been solved or not. For the officers and policemen under their jurisdiction, they should also find out the arrest achievements, fill out the facts and comments separately, and choose the best to recommend and impeach. The director of this bureau will personally review them and give severe punishments and rewards to show the intention of eliminating violence and appeasing the people and comprehensively reviewing the facts. Be careful. This order is attached with the list of kidnapping cases in each district presented by the First Division. May 17, 1930, Director Yuan Liang.
