Local News Two

Public Concession Tram Workers

Welcoming Fellow Workers Released from Prison

Yesterday (the 22nd) at 10:00 AM, all the tram workers from the new and old factories in the Public Concession, acting on a resolution of the Labor Club, began a slowdown. At 10:30 AM, over eighty trams simultaneously gathered at locations like the Hongqiao and Lunjiji Bridge, moving at a walking pace, almost coming to a complete standstill. The ticket selling was also very slow. On the other hand, several dozen workers were sent to the Special District Court to welcome the arrested fellow workers upon their release from prison. At around 1:00 PM, representatives hired two cars to first transport the released workers to the old factory on Hart Road, to receive the welcome of the workers there. Upon arriving at the factory gate, firecrackers were set off for about half an hour. All the coppersmiths stopped working, and over a hundred workers waiting for shifts to start and those selling tickets crowded around the eight released workers, who were ushered into the factory for a meeting. Both sides delivered enthusiastic speeches. Outside the factory, as many as two thousand onlookers showed extreme excitement, applauding to express their welcome. They then boarded the original cars and proceeded to the Huishan Beikaier West Factory, where they received the same expressions of welcome. All the workers from the new and old factories decided to hold a welcoming rally tomorrow (today) at 6:00 PM at the open ground on Dalian Bay Road, while supporting their return to work. The Labor Club will also invite various organizations to participate, which is sure to generate an even more enthusiastic display.

Tram Company

Requesting Probation for Workers

Sincere Cooperation with Workers

On the 14th of this month, at 11:00 AM, when the tram workers' strike had not been resolved, a tram on a certain route, traveling from Yangjingbang to Jing'an Temple, was stopped at the intersection of Avenue Edouard VII and Hart Road by dozens of striking coppersmiths. They damaged the machinery and beat the ticket seller and driver. The driver, Li San'shan, was injured. The police arrested eight people, including Qi Heshang, and sent them to the Special District Local Court for investigation and trial. Now that the labor dispute has been peacefully resolved, the company, hoping that labor and management can sincerely cooperate from now on, also advocates a peaceful resolution for the detained workers. Therefore, when Judge Sun Yuan of the Special District Local Court tried the case yesterday morning, the company sent a Western employee, Mr. Mill, to the court. After Li San'shan and others testified that the defendants had committed violence, he translated that if the judge found the defendants guilty and had to punish them according to the law, he requested leniency and probation. The police lawyer, Bo Liang, also agreed to the Western employee's request. Without defense from the defendants' lawyer, Fan Gang, Judge Sun announced the verdict: Qi Heshang was fined fifty yuan for the crime of obstructing rights and forty yuan for the crime of damage, with the total amount set at sixty yuan. If he could not pay, he would be imprisoned for thirty days. Xu Jinfu, Xu Chunrong, Lin Xingji, Lin Chengshao, Zhang Fushun, Qi Jinsheng, and Zhang Zhikui were each fined forty yuan for the crime of jointly obstructing rights and thirty yuan for the crime of jointly damaging property, with the total amount set at fifty yuan each. The number of days of detention before the judgment was confirmed would be deducted. After the judgment, it was announced that the seven defendants from Xu Jinfu onwards were granted probation for two years.

Zhabei Assassination Case

Liu Zanchen, a Moneylender,

Shot Dead in the Toilet

Four Suspects Arrested

Yesterday morning around 1:00 AM, a man was shot dead in a toilet pit on Jinling Road, Huakang Road, Zhabei. Because the location was remote and the time was late at night, no one knew about it. It was not until 6:40 AM that the patrol leader of the Taiyangmiao Police Station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau discovered it during a patrol. Afterwards, the deceased was identified as Liu Zanchen. The case is very complex, but the main reasons are nothing more than adultery, rivalry, and revenge. Four suspects have now been arrested. The full details are as follows:

A Lecherous Woman: Li Lu'shi, a woman from Yancheng, is forty-six years old and rather plain in appearance. She has always been lecherous. Her late husband, Zhang, passed away almost twenty years ago. Before a month had passed, Lu'shi became acquainted with Zheng Decai, a Funing native who lives at No. 18 Deshunli, Changan Road, and runs a small business (Zheng is also known as Xiao Dezi, fifty-three years old). At first, they were very close and had three sons: the eldest, Shiyi, is thirteen years old; the second, Xiao Erzi, is ten years old; and the youngest, Xiao Sanzi, is also ten years old. However, Li Lu'shi's wild nature was difficult to tame. Over time, her relationship with Zheng gradually faded, eventually abandoning Zheng and forming an inextricable bond with Liu Zanchen.

Cohabiting for Six Years: Liu Zanchen, a native of Beiping, forty-seven years old, resides at No. 96 Jinling Road, Huakang Road, making a living by lending money at high interest rates and is financially well-off. Lu'shi is quite content in his home. Time flies, and it has been six years since they met. Liu pampers her, but he views her former lover, Zheng Decai, as a jealous enemy, and Zheng is filled with hatred, with no opportunity to vent it.

The Reason for Suspicion: Liu has three fellow Yancheng natives living with him: Zhou Shuming, thirty-four years old; Zhou Jihe, thirty-two years old; and Zhou Qicai, thirty years old. They usually get along harmoniously. Qicai's wife, Zhang, is in the prime of her life and has some beauty. The couple is inseparable. Unexpectedly, Qicai suddenly committed a theft last month and was sentenced to five years of forced labor. Zhang, with her husband in prison and struggling to make a living, often relies on Liu for support, leading to jealousy from his peers. They discussed with Zheng, wanting to get rid of Liu to their satisfaction.

Never to Return: The previous night, after Liu Zanchen collected the high-interest money, he gathered with his beloved wife to drink and celebrate. Zhou Shuming and Zhou Jihe, brothers, came to visit. Liu then socialized with them, and the room was filled with joy. Later, when they ran out of cigarettes, Liu went out to buy them, and Zhou and others also followed him out. Who knew that Liu would never return? Li Lu'shi waited for a long time and did not see Liu return. Feeling exhausted, she went to bed first. Little did she know that a tragic scene was about to unfold. A Glimpse of the Gruesome Corpse: Yesterday morning around 9:00 AM, Guo Zhenqi, the patrol leader of the Taiyangmiao Police Station of the Fourth District Headquarters in Zhabei, led a patrol to the toilet at the intersection of Jinling Road and Huakang Road and discovered the body of a man shot dead. The bullet entered from the back right side of his head and exited from the front left temple. The man was tall and strong, wearing a black cloth jacket and trousers, yellow leather shoes, and black socks. Beside him was a waterproof oilcloth umbrella. He was lying on the ground, with blood flowing everywhere, a very gruesome sight. He immediately reported back to the headquarters.

Adultery and Murder: Jin, the head of the Fourth District Headquarters, upon receiving the report, immediately ordered the police chief to cooperate with detectives to investigate and arrest the suspects. They learned that the deceased was named Liu Zanchen and brought Liu's lover, Li Lu'shi, to the station to inquire about the situation. Zheng and others were highly suspected. Zheng Decai, Zhou Shuming, and Zhou Jihe were arrested one after another and interrogated strictly, but all denied the crime. Li Lu'shi swore that Zheng and others committed the murder out of jealousy and adultery. The case was to be investigated and resolved. The body was reported to the Special District Local Court by the local headman at 2:00 PM yesterday. A prosecutor was appointed to conduct an autopsy, confirming that the death was caused by a gunshot wound. The family was instructed to prepare a coffin for burial.

Deputy Comprador of Banque de l'Indochine

Flees with a Huge Sum of Money

Carrying Away 150,000 Taels of Silver

Sends a Letter Promising to Raise Enough Funds for Repayment

Zhu Jixing, a Ningbo native who was the deputy comprador of the Banque de l'Indochine at No. 26, the Bund, Beijing Road, suddenly fled with 150,000 taels of silver the day before yesterday without saying goodbye. By yesterday, Ling, the head comprador of the Banque de l'Indochine, inspected the silver and found a shortage of 150,000 taels of Jiuba standard silver, which greatly surprised him. The deputy comprador, Zhu Jixing, had not arrived at the bank to work by noon. Ling was quite suspicious, so he telephoned Zhu's residence. According to his family, he had not returned home the previous night. The Banque de l'Indochine then went to Zhu's residence at No. 1 Ruihuali to search, but he was long gone. In the afternoon, the bank received a letter in Zhu's own handwriting, stating that although he had taken the money, it was due to temporary financial difficulties and he had no choice. He would return it as soon as he had raised enough funds. It is now reported that the bank, because Zhu had taken such a large sum of money, reported the case to the General Inspectorate of Police for investigation and arrest at 7:00 PM yesterday.

Pirates Break into Songkou

Plundering a Fresh Fish Boat

The Ningbo fishing boat Jin Shunli, loaded with fresh yellow croaker of Xie Alai's fresh fish business from Ningbo, arrived in Wusong the day before yesterday (the 19th) and was docked at the Pudong beach opposite the Jianghai Customs House. Xie immediately went ashore to report to the Jellyfish Guild for assistance in selling the fresh fish. However, due to price issues, they were unable to open the hold and sell the goods. He then went to Shanghai to inquire about market prices. When he returned to Song the next morning to sell the goods, the fresh fish boat was gone. Xie suspected that the boat owner, Jin Shunli, had taken the boat to Shanghai to sell the goods, so he rushed to Shanghai to investigate, but to no avail. In great distress, he returned to Song to inquire. According to boatmen docked there, at around 1:00 AM the previous night, they saw more than a dozen people in a small boat row to the fresh fish boat, then raise the sail and head out to sea. However, it was unknown whether these people were pirates or not. Xie now realized that the pirates were extremely bold and dared to break into Songkou and plunder the fishing boat. Yesterday, the Jellyfish Guild submitted a report to the Fourth District Water Police Department, requesting that a warship be dispatched to pursue and rescue the fresh fish boat and the boat owner Jin Shunli and all eight or nine crew members. According to reports, where the fresh fish boat was docked, dozens of merchant ships often docked overnight. Furthermore, the Shui Jing Junhe, Ce Dian, and Pingyang warships had also been docked there in recent days. Across the street, there was also the Fourth Detachment of the Water Patrol. The pirates seemed to disregard all of this, which can be described as extremely rampant. It is said that three fresh fishing boats sailed out at the same time that night. Other than the Jin Shunli, which has been confirmed, the other two boats cannot be confirmed, and it is possible that they were also pirate ships.

Court Continues Hearing Yesterday

Six Hundred Thousand Yuan Fraud Case

Still Three to Four Hundred Spectators

Besides Lending at High Interest Rates,

The Remaining Sum Was Used for Deposit Interest

He Qiqing Granted Bail to Manage Affairs

Yang Shulin, formerly the patrol chief of the Fourth District of Zhabei, a native of Tianjin, established Wenji Hexing and other companies to specialize in lending money at high interest rates and attracting deposits from all walks of life with high interest rates. Many who coveted ill-gotten gains fell into his trap. Over four or five years, Yang obtained more than 630,000 yuan. To strengthen the depositors' faith, he falsely claimed to start industries and established several shops. By the spring, Yang's fraudulent methods were exposed, and he fled to Tianjin. The depositors sent people to accompany him back to Shanghai and ordered him to settle the accounts. Because Yang wanted to escape again, he was reported to the police, and Yang and his messenger He Qiqing were arrested and sent to the Special District Local Court for interrogation and detention. These events have been reported repeatedly in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the continued hearing of this case. The number of male and female depositors attending the hearing was still three to four hundred. At around 3:00 PM, Judge Sun ascended the bench and interrogated the managers or accountants of Yang's Prida Steel Factory, Hexing Gold Shop, and Wenji Beekeeping Company, one by one, asking about the capital, business conditions, and profits and losses of each shop. He then interrogated the defendant Yang Shulin about what he had done with the huge sum of money. According to Yang, there were still 100,100 yuan of high-interest loans issued by Wenji and 40,000 yuan issued by Hexing, as well as more than 20,000 yuan that could be recovered from associations. The rest was used to pay interest to the depositors, and there were accounts to prove it. The court then asked who handled the high-interest loans. Yang replied that they were all issued by the messengers he hired, of which there were twenty-six. He then reported the names of each person one by one. After mutual arguments by the lawyers of both sides, Judge Sun ordered the defendant He Qiqing to post a bail of 1,000 yuan to manage the accounting affairs outside of detention. Yang Shulin was remanded in custody to await sentencing.

Forged Zhuang Piao

57,000 Yuan

Cannot Escape the Eyes of the Siming Bank

Blank Checks Found on His Person

The Sugar Shop is Already Empty

Zheng Hekang, a native of Yong, was a debt collector at the Deji Sugar Shop at No. 2, Xiang'anli, Rue du Consulat, in the French Concession. The day before yesterday, he presented a Zhuang Piao from the Yifeng Money Shop at No. 26 Ningo Road, worth 57,000 yuan, and three other Zhuang Piao, worth 1,990 yuan, to the Siming Bank for deposit. The bank staff found that one of the Yifeng Zhuang Piao was doubtful, but the rest were genuine. They immediately ordered a clerk to go to the Yifeng Money Shop to verify the authenticity. According to the staff of the money shop, the Zhuang Piao was forged. The bank then detained Zheng and reported the case to the General Inspectorate of Police. Detective Ma Xiaozhi was ordered to arrest Zheng and bring him back to the police station. Three Siming Bank checks were found in Zheng's pocket: (1) silver 31,416 taels, (2) silver 17,700 taels, (3) 3,000 taels, totaling 52,116 taels. The checks were dated for the 1st, 2nd, and 3rd of the month. After investigation, Detective Ma found that Zheng was instigated by the owner of the Deji Sugar Shop to deposit the forged Zhuang Piao and withdraw the money with the three checks. He then went to the Deji Sugar Shop with the French Concession police detectives to arrest the accomplices. Unexpectedly, when they arrived at the shop, they found no one inside, and the bedding was rolled up. The account box was also empty. He returned to report to the police chief, who ordered Zheng to be detained. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Criminal Court of the Special District Court. Chief Judge Xu Jiashi and Chief Prosecutor Zhou Xianjue ascended the bench for the trial. The police lawyer, Gan Jingxian, presented the case, stating that the defendant was accused of fraud under Article 363 of the Criminal Law and requested prosecution. He then presented the forged Zhuang Piao as evidence. Detective Ma and the representatives of the Yifeng Money Shop, Shi Huiting, and the Siming Bank, Tong Xueyin, successively submitted all the details. When questioned, the defendant confessed that he was instructed by his master, Zhu, and did not know that the Zhuang Piao was forged. After Judge Xu verified the confession, he ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody for further questioning at a later date.

Goods Ordered and Goods Not Ordered

Sandalwood Prices Differ

The Difference in Price Between

Ordered Goods and Non-Ordered Goods is Four Taels

The Point of Contention is Whether It Was a One-Time Purchase

In June of the previous year, Chen Maotang ordered 30 tons of sandalwood from the Sino-Australian Trading Company at No. 24 Sijing Road. Not long after, the goods arrived, totaling 47 tons and 13.5 dans. Chen purchased them all and made a considerable profit after selling them. The company then claimed that Chen had only ordered 30 tons, which should be calculated at the agreed price of 16 taels and 5 qian. The remaining 17 tons and 13.5 dans should be calculated at the market price of 20 taels and 5 qian. Therefore, they demanded that Chen return 1,612 taels of silver. Chen argued that although he had said he would order 30 tons, he had immediately agreed to the company's request to purchase all 47 tons and settled the account in one transaction. How could it be divided into two matters? Therefore, he sternly refused the company's request to return the money. The Sino-Australian Company then, in the name of a British merchant, hired a lawyer to sue Chen in the former Provisional Court for not paying the money. At that time, the court had not yet been reorganized, and foreign consuls could sit on the bench for cases involving Chinese and foreigners. Unexpectedly, the case was not concluded before the Special District Local Court was reorganized, and the consular jury system was abolished. Lawsuits, regardless of Chinese or foreign, were treated equally. Those who relied on foreign merchants as protection lost their effectiveness. The Sino-Australian Trading Company then authorized the comprador, Zhou Rulin, to hire a Chinese lawyer to participate in the lawsuit. The reason was that Zhou and Chen were involved in the transaction and Zhou was aware of all the circumstances. Therefore, he was participating to assist the plaintiff. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenyong opened the court for the trial. Only the participant of the plaintiff, the British Sino-Australian Trading Company, was present. The defendant hired lawyer Wang Fushang to defend him. Lawyer Wang first stated the reason why the plaintiff company was now represented by its comprador, saying that it was due to the change in the court system and the fact that consuls could no longer sit on the bench. He then explained the conflict in the case, arguing that the goods were actually purchased in one transaction and that the plaintiff was forcing a division into two batches and needed to provide evidence to prove it. The lawyer of the plaintiff participant then stated that the defendant had only ordered 30 tons and was in partnership with Zhou Weixin. The remaining 17 tons and 13.5 dans, because they arrived at the same time as the 30

Page 16

The Republic of China, May 23, 1920 (Shen Bao, Fourth Page) Friday (16)

tons, were also sold to the defendant. Since they were not within the ordered quantity, the price should not be the same as the ordered price. Now, the prices of the two batches of goods are combined, and after deducting the money received, 1,612 taels are owed, requesting a judgment for repayment and overdue interest. Judge Xu, because the plaintiff had not arrived in court, ordered a postponement and summons for the Western plaintiff to continue the trial.

A Fierce Wife Abuses Her Elders

Xu Longchui Requests a Divorce

Four Witnesses All Testify to Her Ferocity

Xu Longsheng, a farmer from Xijiao, the 30th Bao, 3rd Tu, Xujiazhai Township, complained that his wife, Xu Zhang, was extremely ferocious, even to the point of abusing his elders, which he could no longer tolerate. He recently hired lawyer Chen Wenxiang to file a petition in the Local Court, requesting a divorce. Yesterday morning, Judge Du Xian opened the court for questioning. The plaintiff, Xu Longsheng, testified that he was twenty-five years old, a native of Shanghai, and made a living by farming. He had married the defendant, Zhang, but she was ferocious and quarrelsome, often picking fights and twisting and beating him. His mother tried to intervene and was slapped in the face. Under these circumstances, it was difficult to live together, and he requested that a divorce be granted. The defendant, Xu Zhang, testified that she was twenty-seven years old and had been married for eight years. She had a mother and elder brother at home. The court asked why she beat her husband and mother-in-law. She replied, "I didn't beat him. They were beating me. My sister-in-law from next door came to break it up." The court ordered (1) witness Xu Ziting to testify. He was thirty-five years old. The court ordered the defendant to identify who Xu was. She replied, "He is my uncle." The court asked Xu Ziting why they were in court. He replied, "On March 13th of this year, Longsheng went fishing, and the defendant wouldn't let him, leading to a dispute. I saw the defendant beat the plaintiff. Because the plaintiff is usually afraid of the defendant, the defendant's ferocity has become more and more intense." The court then ordered (2) witness Zhou Fangyu to testify. The defendant identified him as her uncle-in-law. Zhou testified that the defendant had beaten her husband more than once. Because the plaintiff is gentle and timid, he was beaten by the defendant. His aunt tried to intervene and was even beaten. The court also ordered (2) witness Xu Xiaomao to testify. The defendant identified him as her uncle. Xu testified that he and the plaintiff lived in the same house. The couple often quarreled and fought, and the defendant even beat her mother-in-law. The court also ordered (4) witness Chen Deshun to testify, stating that the plaintiff was his nephew and his testimony was the same as above. Xu Zhang, fifty-five years old, testified that the defendant, Xu Zhang, was her daughter-in-law. They were not on good terms. At night, her son tried to sleep in the room, but the daughter-in-law locked the door first, not allowing her son to sleep in the room. She tried to persuade her, but she scolded her and even slapped her. She was really having a hard time. If she didn't beat her, she wouldn't bother the magistrate. Her son was a good man and was used to being bullied by her. Beating and scolding were not uncommon. The court questioned and then questioned the defendant, with the witnesses present all saying she was bad. Had she ever beaten her mother-in-law? She replied, "No." The court then ordered both parties to withdraw and wait for the defendant's mother and elder brother to be summoned to court for further trial.

A Woman Accuses Her Husband of Abandonment

An Appeal Causes Problems

The Plaintiff Failed to Appear on Time

The Initial Judgment Was Dismissed

Restoration to the Original State is Impossible

The Court Ordered Further Investigation Before Retrial

Niu Qu, a local woman residing at No. 802 Dahaili, Yuezhou Road, hired lawyer Lu Qi to file a criminal complaint in the Special District Local Court against her husband, Niu Shanqing, for abandonment. The gist of her complaint was that the plaintiff married the defendant in September of the 16th year of the Republic [1927], and they were initially on good terms. However, because the defendant repeatedly asked her to borrow money from her mother's family and was unsuccessful, their relationship deteriorated. The defendant squandered almost all of the plaintiff's dowry. Last spring, the defendant had other plans and left without saying goodbye, leaving the plaintiff's livelihood uncared for and resorting to sinister means. On March 23rd of last year, he went to the defendant's former mother-in-law, Ding Jin, to demand living expenses from the defendant. Unexpectedly, upon meeting, he insulted and scolded the plaintiff. He then agreed to give the plaintiff (hereinafter referred to as "the plaintiff") 30 yuan per month as living expenses, but a contract had to be signed, with no increases in the future. The plaintiff unknowingly agreed, and the defendant wrote two copies of the contract, forcing her to sign. Later, the plaintiff showed the contract to others and realized that it was not a contract for monthly payments but a divorce document. From then on, the defendant never met her again. The plaintiff had no choice but to complain to the Women's Association and hire a lawyer to publish a denial in the newspaper and issue a warning, ordering the return of the forged document within a time limit to avoid litigation. However, the defendant ignored it. Therefore, the plaintiff filed a lawsuit requesting the defendant be punished under Articles 224, 310, and 318 of the Criminal Law. This case was tried twice by the court. During the second hearing, Niu Qu was absent without reason. The presiding judge ruled that the case was dismissed, and the defendant was ordered to return. The plaintiff, dissatisfied with the judgment, filed an appeal. Yesterday afternoon, Song Yuan, the presiding judge of the Criminal Division of the High Court, Du Fuyao, Ye Zaizhou, and Chief Prosecutor Wang Zhennan held a joint hearing. The appellee, Niu Shanqing, was absent. The appellant's lawyer, Lu Qi, stated the reasons for disagreeing with the initial judgment, saying that when the Special Court held the second hearing on April 23rd, Niu Qu received the summons but, because the word "court" on the summons was unclear, she went to the Fifth Court to wait for the hearing. Unexpectedly, the case was being heard in the Third Court. After the lawyer found her, he accompanied her to the Third Court at 2:20 PM, but the case had already been decided by the judge. The lawyer immediately requested restoration to the original state, but the presiding judge refused and ordered an appeal for remedy. Therefore, the appeal was filed. He then presented the summons as evidence. Judge Song then reviewed the initial trial records and declared that there was no record of the lawyer's request for restoration to the original state in the records. Therefore, it would be better for the lawyer to withdraw the appeal and request the initial court to restore the original state. Lawyer Lu replied that the lawyer had indeed made the request at the time, but whether it was recorded or not was up to the court, and the deadline for requesting restoration to the original state was seven days. If the court's suggestion was followed, the deadline would have passed. What should be done? Judge Song then ordered a postponement for further investigation before retrial.

Son Goes Mad, Livelihood Cut Off

Old Woman Attempts Suicide by Drowning

Yesterday afternoon around 4:00 PM, an elderly woman over fifty years old boarded a ferry at the Jiangtian Wharf in the Sixteenth Block to cross the river. When the boat reached the middle of the river, the woman suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. After her body sank, it suddenly floated back up. The ferry crew rescued her and took her to Pudong, where she was handed over to the police, who took her to the Third District Public Security Bureau. She identified herself as Zhang Zhang, fifty-two years old, from Qingjiang, residing at No. 2 Derunli, Shanghai Ning Station. She had a married son and a six-year-old grandson. Her son, Shaoqi, twenty-eight years old, was a driver for the Huashang Tram Company, earning a monthly salary of only twenty yuan, which barely provided for the family. Unfortunately, Shaoqi recently became mentally ill, lost his normalcy, and was unable to work. He is now being treated in a hospital. As a result, the family's livelihood was cut off, and she was starving to death. Therefore, she did not want to linger in the world and would rather drown herself. Having made up her mind, she left home alone at 3:00 PM today while her daughter-in-law was out washing clothes. She originally intended to drown herself in the Suzhou Creek, but because the water was shallow, she feared she would not die. Therefore, she changed her mind and sought death in the Huangpu River. Chief Zhang, upon hearing her statement and seeing her pitiful condition, ordered that relatives be found and notified to claim her.

Health Campaign Opens Yesterday

The Health Campaign Exhibition jointly organized by the Shanghai YMCA and YWCA opened yesterday. The venue was filled with many exhibits. The Municipal Health Bureau also sent specialists to display various specimens. After 10:00 AM, visitors flocked in, and the afternoon was particularly crowded. Women, infants, and members of various groups enthusiastically came to have their physical examinations. The YWCA was responsible for the physical examinations of women and children yesterday, and those who came for examinations were very enthusiastic. City Government

Commendation for Mother and Daughter Who Died Saving Aunt

Exemplary Filial Piety of the Zhang Family

Shanghai Special Municipality Branch Security Bureau Chief Yuan Liang, previously reported a case where three members of a household, including a woman named Zhang Wangshi, were burned to death due to negligence at No. 4 Ankang Lane, Second District, Second Precinct. After receiving the phone report from the precinct, he immediately ordered an investigation into the ages, origins, and circumstances of the victims before submitting a report for review. Now, according to the report submitted by Precinct Chief Meng Quansun, Zhang Wangshi and her daughter, Cuifeng, were downstairs when the fire broke out. Because their aunt, Zhang Liushi, was bedridden due to paralysis, the mother and daughter rushed upstairs to rescue her, resulting in the three of them, grandmother, granddaughter, and daughter-in-law, perishing in the flames. Firefighters discovered their bodies together in a corner, a truly tragic sight. It was also learned that Zhang Liushi was in her sixties and had been paralyzed for many years. Her son, Zhang Bochen, was a businessman in Tianjin, and Zhang Wangshi was responsible for all household affairs, serving her mother-in-law with filial piety, which was universally praised. Most notably, despite Zhang Liushi's paralysis for years, Zhang Wangshi consistently cared for her, administering medicine and tending to her needs, which was highly commended by the neighbors. Her daughter, Cuifeng, had attended Qingzhen Girls' Elementary School and was not only raised by her mother's teachings but also influenced by her teachers, enabling her to deeply understand righteousness. She followed her mother to rescue her grandmother, resulting in their simultaneous death. The three bodies were carried downstairs by the firefighters and were fortunately mostly intact, with only slight scorching on the fingers and toes. Their relative, Wangshi, had already purchased coffins and arranged for their temporary storage at the Jingjiang Public Hall. Zhang Liushi was sixty years old, Zhang Wangshi was thirty-nine years old, and Zhang Cuifeng was seventeen years old, all registered in Shanghai. After reviewing the report, Yuan noted that Zhang Wangshi had already been downstairs before the fire and was in a safe location. However, out of concern for her sick aunt, she disregarded the dangerous flames and rushed back to save her. Her daughter, Cuifeng, eagerly joined her, their actions motivated by deep affection and disregard for their own safety, resulting in their tragic demise. Their deeds were worthy of special recognition and encouragement. Therefore, he first presented them with a plaque inscribed with the four characters "Exemplary Filial Piety" for immediate display. He also submitted a report to the municipal government, requesting a generous commendation to inspire moral behavior and comfort the souls of the departed. Mayor Zhang Qun, after reviewing the report, approved the granting of a plaque inscribed with the four characters "Teach Filial Piety and Encourage Moral Customs" as a commendation.

Water Police

Capture of Pirate Leader Shen Qinggang

Large numbers of pirates have repeatedly appeared in the waters off Wusongkou and the counties of Chongming and Qiqi, landing to loot residents' property. Zhu Bingzheng, the Fourth District Chief of the Wusong Water Police, dispatched a large team of water police to suppress them. However, the pirate ships had already fled upon hearing the news. Subsequently, Zhu Fukuan, the Squad Leader of the Seventeenth Platoon of the district, learned that the pirate leader, Shen Qinggang, was hiding in the Xin'an Town area. He secretly went to the location around 4 PM the previous afternoon and apprehended Shen, taking him to the Seventeenth Platoon headquarters. Under questioning by Platoon Leader Gong Jinqin, Shen confessed that he was thirty-five years old, from Haizhou, and had over a hundred followers and many sailing ships. He stated that all the robberies were planned and directed by him and that his second-in-command, Lu Qinglang, was currently in charge of everything on the pirate ships, whereabouts unknown. He also admitted that the recent robberies of merchant ships, such as the Dachangli and Fengxiang, were also orchestrated by him. After receiving the confession, Platoon Leader Gong immediately telegraphed District Chief Zhu for approval and transferred Shen to the Chongming County government for trial.

Dispute Among Tea Servers on the New Jiangtian Steamer

The Reason: A Dispute Over Rooms

The two hundred-plus tea servers on the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's New Jiangtian steamer, which operates between Shanghai and Ningbo, have long had disagreements. They are divided into two factions: one affiliated with the Seamen's Union and the other with the Anli Union (now renamed the Shanghai-Ningbo Union). Recently, the opinions of both sides have become increasingly extreme, stemming from a dispute over rooms. All the rooms on the steamer are assigned by the business director, with no inherent bias. However, the Shanghai-Ningbo faction intentionally made things difficult for the other faction (Seamen's Union). A fight broke out between the two sides in Ningbo the day before yesterday. Yesterday, after the steamer arrived in Shanghai, a dispute erupted again around 4 PM between the Shanghai-Ningbo factions. The steamer director tried to dissuade them to no avail, and they even attempted to assault him. The police were notified and arrived to arrest several dozen people from both sides. Around 5 PM, someone named Jin mediated a resolution, and the situation was diffused. The steamer's departure was reportedly delayed by about an hour.

Nephew Accused of Seizing Inheritance

Two Daughters Grown Up and Suing for Return of Property

Li Guisong, a villager from He Wangzhai in the Jiangwan District, passed away due to illness on October 29, 1926. His wife also died on December 16 of the same year. Li had no sons, only three daughters. The second daughter was adopted by another family. Now, only two daughters remain: the eldest, Lin Nan, and the youngest, Yin Nan, both of whom were young children at the time. Their inheritance was managed by their nephew, Jiang Shisheng (son of Li Guisong's older sister). Now that Lin Nan and Yin Nan have grown up, they requested a division of the inheritance, but Jiang refused. Lin Nan and Yin Nan hired lawyer Qu Yue to sue Jiang Shisheng in the district court for seizing the inheritance and refusing to return it. The lawsuit stated that after their father, Li Guisong, passed away, he left behind twenty-one mu of fertile land, five houses, over twenty dan of cotton, and fifteen dan of wheat, totaling approximately seven to eight thousand yuan. They requested that, as biological daughters, they be returned all of the inheritance to manage it themselves. Yesterday morning, Judge Tong Shenglü held a hearing. The plaintiffs, Li Lin Nan, Li Yin Nan, Sun Bingfa (as Yin Nan's representative), and the lawyer Qu Yue hired by the plaintiffs, all appeared in court. The plaintiffs testified about the previous events. The judge, noting the defendant's absence, did not open the debate and ordered that the defendant be summoned to court again for a joint review.

Hotel Owner Accused of Fraud

Even When the Hotel Could Not Be Maintained, He Still Collected Deposits From Tea Servers

The Plaintiffs Wept Bitterly

Ji Zhongwen, the owner of the Huizhong Hotel in Tong'an Lane on Hankou Road, was recently sued in the Special District Court by the entire staff, Cao Zhongyun, Xu Quangen, Du Atao, Xu Aquan, Ling Jinlin, and twenty others, who hired a lawyer to file criminal charges against Ji for fraud. After being sued, Ji also hired a lawyer to sue Du, Xu, and Ling for illegally detaining his son, Shen　, using violence and infringing on his freedom. The two cases were previously summoned once, but were postponed due to the hope of a settlement. However, Ji Zhongwen had no sincere intention of settling, leading to a breakdown. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Cheng Shangfeng of the Special District Court continued the hearing in the fifth courtroom. In the case against Ji Zhongwen, thirteen plaintiffs appeared, electing Cao Zhongxue as their representative. Cao stated that he was over sixty years old and worked as an accountant with Xu Quangen. The rest were tea servers who had collectively paid deposits of 3,530 yuan to Ji. However, Ji did not hand over the money to the accountant but secretly took it home for his own use. The hotel was owned solely by Ji, who had leased it from someone for 6,000 yuan in early February last year, with a monthly rent of 430 yuan. The hotel was now sealed because it owed the landlord, Hartung, seven months' rent, totaling 3,000 yuan. All of their clothes and belongings were locked inside, leaving them without food or shelter. He expressed feeling oppressed by the landlord's power, speaking with tears in his eyes, a truly pitiful sight. Judge Cheng asked Cao why they didn't try to maintain the business. Cao replied that although the hotel's assets were worth 6,000 yuan, they had once discussed having someone named Yao continue the business, agreeing to pay the 3,000 yuan rent. However, the landlord demanded a large commission, and after repeated pleading, they reduced it to 900 yuan. Yao paid 900 yuan in cash and issued a check for 3,000 yuan. However, the landlord insisted on cash, and the deal fell through. The plaintiff's lawyer argued that Ji continued to collect deposits even when he could not maintain the business, constituting fraudulent behavior. Now that Ji has fled, they requested an arrest warrant. After reviewing the evidence, Judge Cheng ruled that the case of Ji Zhongwen suing Du, Xu, and Ling was not accepted. The case against Ji Zhongwen was postponed for seven days for another hearing.

Russian Upset Over Death of a Dog

Cross-Border Police Car Crushes a Puppy

Russian Could Not Bear It and Stepped Forward to Beat

The Cross-Border Police No. 223 of the French Concession was driving a car at around 6 PM the previous afternoon. When passing Avenue du Père Huc by Avenue Joffre, it almost hit a puppy on the side of the road. A Russian named Garmen, witnessing this and feeling indignant, stepped forward and, without asking what happened, struck the Cross-Border Police in the face with the musical instrument he was carrying, causing him to bleed. A patrolman arrived and took the Russian into custody at the police station. Yesterday, he was sent to the French Court for questioning. The plaintiff first complained about the beating. A witness named Zhao Wanjin testified that he saw the defendant commit the assault. The defendant, represented by lawyer Mutiyi, argued that the defendant was genuinely upset by what he saw and acted out of momentary anger, therefore he stepped forward to intervene. The defendant was usually well-behaved and had never argued with anyone. This was his first offense, and he requested leniency. The Chinese and Western judge ruled that the defendant should not have committed the assault and fined him ten yuan, with a one-year suspended sentence, and ordered him to compensate the plaintiff for ten taels of silver.

Public Concession

Problem of House Numbering

New Style Numbering Method

Adopting a Gradual Approach

The Municipal Council Gazette stated that the Council had previously appointed Mr. Barker, Mr. Zhou Pingxian (transliteration), Mr. Pant, Mr. Johnson, and Mr. Allen to form a special committee to discuss adopting a new house numbering method for new and old roads within the concession that needed renumbering. After several meetings, and a detailed review of the current methods and reports from various offices of the Council and other parties, the results of the deliberations are detailed below:

The committee felt that there was a need to improve the current numbering method, but it did not advocate for a complete overhaul immediately, as this would lead to a huge increase in expenses and cause various inconveniences to the residents. Moreover, address information on various communication documents, insurance policies, name registers, etc., would need to be changed, and various public and private organizations would face unnecessary work. In several roads within the concession, house numbers were not in order due to the frequent renovations or additions of buildings. The committee believed that it was necessary to change these, but only when absolutely necessary. However, roads such as Jing'an Temple Road, Tongfu Road, Medhurst Road, Jiangxi Road, and Ningbo Road, which had extremely disorganized house numbers, needed to be changed immediately. The committee strongly supported adopting the Council's previously proposed method of odd-even numbering. This method involved placing odd and even numbers in close proximity, facing each other, with a spacing of twelve feet per number being the most appropriate. In the future, when buildings were added alongside the roads, there would be no need for further changes. Numbering the numerous and disorganized alleys within the concession was particularly difficult. The best solution was to assign each alley a number, with the numbers continuing sequentially from the adjacent buildings. The houses within the alleys would be assigned additional numbers, with even numbers on the right and odd numbers on the left, to ensure clarity. The current method of adding letters was best suited for houses in alleys. According to the above methods, postal communication could be addressed on main roads as "Mr. So-and-so, So-and-so Road, So-and-so Road," and within alleys as "Mr. So-and-so, So-and-so Lane, So-and-so Number, So-and-so Road." The committee also felt that it would be more appropriate to call alleys "branch roads" rather than "lanes." The practice of having separate numbering systems for Western-style and Chinese-style buildings on roads within the concession should be abolished. The house numbering method should be consistent across all roads, with north-south roads numbered from the south end, with odd numbers on the east side and even numbers on the west side. East-west roads should be numbered from the east end, with odd numbers on the south side and even numbers on the north side. However, the numbering system for roads in the eastern district of the concession should be an exception, with numbering progressing from west to east, as the numbering of houses on all roads generally expanded outward from the center of the city. Mr. Baker had previously submitted opinions on the house numbering method, and the committee asked him to explain everything. Mr. Baker attended the meeting on April 10 and delivered a very long speech. The committee members only reviewed it in detail. In summary, the committee believed that all the proposals were suitable for the current situation. It was proposed that this method be used as a guide for the future, as each number would occupy twelve feet of space and would be permanent, without the need for further changes. However, this method should be implemented first on roads where renumbering was necessary, with the rest being implemented gradually. A full implementation should take several years to minimize inconvenience to the residents.

Wall Collapse During Demolition

House Collapses

Around 4 PM yesterday, during the demolition of the high wall on the west side of the old site of the Great Southeast Tobacco Company in Taihe Lane, Nan Chujiaqiao, Avenue de la Marne, French Concession, the wall suddenly collapsed due to incomplete procedures, causing part of the houses and piled firewood of the Laoganyan firewood and charcoal depot at No. 167 Rue Glocque to collapse. The police detained the demolition foreman for questioning.

Under Despotic Marriage

Chen Lindi Commits Suicide by Taking Opium

Fiancé of Inferior Talent and Appearance

Father Kills Daughter's Life

Chen Lifeng, residing at No. 5 and a half Guangxi Road, is over forty years old and works at a certain cinema. He has a daughter named Lindi, who is twenty-nine years old and still unmarried. Chen was eager to fulfill his long-held wish without consulting his daughter and hastily arranged a marriage with a certain son. Upon learning of this and discovering that her fiancé was of inferior talent and appearance and suffered from poverty, she was constantly worried. Chen remained unaware. As the wedding date approached, he specially prepared wedding attire for her. As time was running out and she could not change the situation, Lindi had a death wish. Early the previous morning, she secretly swallowed opium paste. When discovered, she was rushed to Guangren Hospital for treatment, but the poisoning was too severe. She died at 9 PM that night. The Zhabei police station received a report and sent detectives to transport the body to the Fielun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, they reported to the Special District Court and requested that Prosecutor Guo come to the morgue for an examination. He sat in the public position and questioned the deceased's parents before ordering Chen Lifeng to sign a statement and claim the body for coffin burial.

Green Garden

Establishment of National Jinan University Bank

The original school bank of National Jinan University was established, but its scale was small, and its finances were confused with those of the university, leading to many malpractices. Therefore, President Zheng strived to improve it. In addition to handing over all the university's finances to accountant Pan Xulun for management, he also hired several other committee members to prepare for the establishment of the Jinan University Bank. It is completely independent, separated from the university's finances, and its business scope and procedures are exactly the same as ordinary commercial banks. All kinds of trust, remittance, current, and fixed deposits and loans are within the scope of its business. Not only teachers and students of the university can do business with the bank, but all villagers in the Zhenru area are sincerely welcome to do business with the bank. Among the staff, the general manager is Ye Yuanjun, and the directors are President Zheng, Vice President Hong, Dean Yang, and a dozen or so giants from Shanghai banks. It is reported that the capital is prepared to raise 500,000 yuan, and 200,000 to 300,000 yuan has already been raised. The bank is located within Jinan University, and students from the Jinan University Business School can practice in the bank every day. The bank can hire fewer employees and save expenses, while students can gain more experience and be better prepared for future work. It is truly a win-win situation. The bank opened yesterday, and Manager Ye prepared tea and refreshments to welcome guests to visit and report on the organization process. He also welcomed the villagers of Zhenru to understand the meaning of saving, not to waste money, to save surplus money, and to deposit it in the bank for emergencies. It is said that the villagers of Zhenru, under the guidance of the students of the university, have more knowledge than other villagers and have always trusted the university very much. They will definitely transfer their trust in the university to the bank, and the development of the bank is just beginning. (Mu Bu Jing)

The Problem of the Role of Cyrano · Jun

The news of the Fudan Drama Society's rehearsal of Cyrano has been publicized for a long time, and many friends who love drama and art have been looking forward to it for many days. However, they have not yet announced a definite date for the public performance, so there are various speculations from the outside world. According to the latest news I know about Cyrano, there have been some changes from before. I will truthfully report it as follows to comfort the friends who are waiting for Cyrano.

The role of Cyrano in the play is the most important role in the entire play. It was originally played by Hong Shen, the director of the society, himself. The play has already been rehearsed for one act. Later, because Hong Jun felt that his responsibility for the entire play was extremely important, and he also played the lead role, he was afraid of neglecting one thing or another. Coincidentally, Ma Yanxiang, an old classmate of the school, had just returned to Shanghai from Guangdong. Hong Jun decided to let Ma Jun play the role of Cyrano. Ma Jun has been engaged in the Chinese drama movement for a long time and is rich in acting experience. He will definitely make us satisfied with this role. In addition, the role of Roxane, the female lead in the play, was reportedly played by Chen Chenying, the wife of Ma Yanxiang, when the play was decided to be rehearsed last year. Later, Ms. Chen left Shanghai, so Jin Zhongyu, who was famous for playing "Parasitic Grass," was invited to replace her. However, Ms. Jin was unable to accept the role for some reason, so it was finally decided that Liang Peishu would play the role. There are rumors that Yu Zhaobi will play the role, but that is just speculation.

The play is now being rehearsed day and night in the Zibin Academy of the school. According to Hong Shen, the director of the society, it is expected to be performed around June 10.

Love Causes a War of Words

The School of Social Sciences of C University moved to Zhabei from W last year. Its dormitory is located on the only route for students commuting to N Girls' School. In this sunny weather with bright spring and easily moved spring feelings, it is of course inevitable that students from the two schools will convey their feelings through eye contact, gradually to correspondence, and achieve the so-called result of love.

At first, only Mr. L of C University and Ms. L of N Girls' School had a passionate love. However, in just half a year, there are now more than a dozen lovers. According to my personal investigation, it is true that the infectiousness of love is just like the infectiousness of Shanghai fashion. I only regret that Ala did not live in that dormitory, otherwise, maybe there would be an object too.

In the eyes of the principal of N Girls' School, of course, this is detrimental to the school spirit. In order to prevent the spread of the love craze among students of the two schools, she specifically wrote a letter to the president of N University, saying in brief, "...The school spirit of our school has always been well-known in Shanghai. Since your school moved here, many love affairs have occurred, which seems to be caused by the lax discipline of your school. Your school should be relocated immediately to benefit both parties..."

The authorities of C University specifically brought this matter up for discussion at the school affairs meeting and decided to answer like this, "...Our school's students have always strictly abided by the rules in W. Only after being adjacent to your school did such unfortunate events occur, which clearly your school should be blamed for. Your school is specially requested to relocate as soon as possible to avoid harming the studies of students from both sides..."

After this letter was sent, N Girls' School reportedly replied with a letter with even more severe wording. C University is preparing to deal with it through legal procedures. If it is not resolved soon, it is feared that the turmoil will escalate. As for who should move, this is of course a matter for the Shanghai court, but there is no explicit provision in the law and no precedent to follow. I am a bit embarrassed for the judge. I still hope that it will not be resolved in court. (Ma Fangzhai)

'Red-Headed Woman'

University movie fever, this is really the leap of youth.

Student Soldiers Mutiny · Xi

Who doesn't know that the Fudan Student Army was established before the May 3rd Massacre? Who doesn't know that the Fudan Student Army went to Hangzhou twice to show off? The regiment commander, Dong Yuanqing, was indeed very enthusiastic, and the coach, Zhou Jiada, was indeed very serious. When Minister Shi Zhaoji came to inspect last year, he thought he was very satisfied and praised him greatly. This year, the training of new recruits continued as before, and the spirit was very good, but unexpectedly, a mutiny occurred a few days ago. The reason was that the dew on the grass in the morning was not dry, and they had to kneel down to aim during training. Regiment Commander Dong believed that the soldiers were unwilling to serve, and resigned to the president in anger.

The Story of World Literature (I) (V) (IX) Translated by Hu Zhongchi, written by John Macy of America

Chapter 40: The Classical Age of German Literature

Just like Arnold and Emerson and Morley, whether we know it ourselves or not, we are all disciples of Goethe. Any liberal person who comes into contact with this master will understand that becoming his disciple is inevitable. Rather than moral formalism, it is to unite the moral energy; rather than international antagonism, it is to unite the world; and in literature, life, politics, and thought, it is to cultivate the essence of things in the face of the value of myth. Anyone can draw infinite inspiration and strength and light from this one person's life, model, writing, or even the letters and short satires he wrote occasionally.

Goethe is a great poet, but he is far more than that. Some of his formal works, such as the novels "Wilhelm Meister's Apprenticeship" and "Elective Affinities," and some of his dramas, are not the easiest reads in today's world. What compensates for this fact is that he is infinitely more than a poet.

When Goethe was young, he was a student of Gottsched and the French style in Leipzig and wrote the love poems of the Anacreontic style that were customary at the time. He went from Leipzig to Strasbourg, where he met Herder, who enlightened him about the treasures of folk poetry. Almost overnight, he became a first-class lyric poet. Then came the Shakespeare worship craze, the age of decadence and the romantic sorrow of "Storm and Stress." This was manifested by the novel "The Sorrows of Young Werther," which swept across Europe and earned Goethe international fame at the age of twenty-four.

Page 24

May 23, 1920 (Shen Bao Edition)

This promising young man was invited to the court of Weimar. There, although there were short intervals from time to time, he spent his long life. He took the draft of the first part of "Faust" to Weimar. He completed the second part there sixty-five years later. Then came busy and annoying years, a retreat to Italy, and the classical age. During this time, he wrote the dramas "Iphigenia," "Torquato Tasso," etc., the gorgeous Venetian-style satires, and the delicate pastoral poem "Hermann and Dorothea." His middle age and old age until extreme old age were devoted to politics, the development of the theater, physical and biological science, the writing of autobiographies, and the completion of "Faust." However, in all periods of his life, there was an uninterrupted stream of lyric poetry. This stream, in scope, passion, wisdom, and music, has not been surpassed by any other poet.

No matter what he was doing, he never forgot "Faust." He started writing the drama when he was twenty-three and completed it when he was eighty-three. It is filled with the incomparable spiritual inspiration and wisdom of his mind. The story is extremely simple. Faust is a scholar who yearns for life. He knows that salvation lies not in theory but in experience. Under the guidance of Mephistopheles, the spirit of negation and evil, he throws himself into the world of living experience. He tries wild pleasure, carnal love, power, and assimilation with classical antiquity. All these experiences still do not give him satisfaction. He finds ultimate satisfaction in the most simple and practical service to his fellow men. However, this is only a stage in his pursuit; it is not the goal. The path itself is the goal. Life is its own purpose and must be justified from within. Completion is beyond the realm we can reach. We do not know what it is, but in fact, to the human mind, it is very similar to stagnation and death. From this point of view, our highest achievement is noble effort, a tireless creative life. It is that which saves Faust and defeats Mephistopheles, and it is the affirmation of that truth that welcomes Faust into the eternal army.
